به، وقد أخرج الطبراني في خبر التحول أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قال: «أولئك رجال آمنوا بالغيب» فلم يعتبر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أخبار الواحد خبراً وحكم بإيمانهم بالغيب وهذا إنكار للطريق فلا يقوم حجة، ويجاب في «التحرير» عن الثاني بعث الآحاد لتبليغ نواسخ القاطع ممنوع من ادعى فعليه البيان فافهم (و) قالوا (ثالثاً) قال الله تعالى: ﴿قُل لَا أَجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَى مُحَرَّمًا عَلَى طَاعِمٍ يَطْعَمُهُ إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَمًا مَّسْفُوحًا أَوْ لَحْم خنزير ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٤٥] الآية: نسخ بتحريم كل ذي ناب من السباع من أن التحريم إنما ثبت بخبر الواحد وحمله على التخصيص) دون النسخ (كما قيل بعيد) لكونه متراخياً عنه، فإن الآية مكية، وهذا التحريم كان بالمدينة والتراخي في المخصص باطل عندنا مطلقاً، وعند غيرنا عن وقت الحاجة (قلنا) لا نسخ إذ (المعنى لا أجد (الآن إذا المضارع ظاهر في الحال ولو تنزل فمحتمل له فيحمل عليه فلا رفع التحريم الاستقبال لعدم المعارضة (ولو سلم) الارتفاع فعدم الوجدان إنما يوجب إباحة أصلية. فإن لزم رفع هذه الإباحة (فرفع الإباحة الأصلية ليس بنسخ فتدبر ) قال في الحاشية الفرق بين هذا التقرير مشكل في إثبات حكم شرعي والجواب عنه أن ههنا أخباراً بعدم وجدان النص، وهو إنما يوجب عدم تعلق الخطاب بالتحريم وأما تعلقه بالإباحة فكلا بخلاف التقرير فإنه دال على تعلق الخطاب بالإباحة فافهم ومنع ابن الحاجب التحريم أي تحريم السباع من البهائم فلا نسخ إنما هو لأنه مالكي) والسباع من البهائم سوى الخنزير مباحة عنده .
The first principle: The book (says): The common feature between conjectural (rulings) is that strength and weakness in the amount of conjecture are not considered, contrary to what is reasonable, unless it is said: its consideration is a kind of difficulty and thus falls, but there is (something) in it. Except that it has a certain strength close to certainty, like the well-known (reports) according to the Hanafis, which oppose the mutawatir and by which abrogation through addition is permissible. We have an investigation concerning it which we will mention if God wills. They said: First: The direction to the House (the Kaaba) was established after its being cut off, i.e., after the decisive ruling of direction to Jerusalem was established through the report of a single caller (for the people of the mosque of Quba). So they turned to the House after they had been facing Jerusalem, and the Messenger of God (peace be upon him and his family and companions) did not deny it. Malik, al-Bukhari, Muslim, and al-Nasa'i narrated from Ibn 'Umar: While the people were at Quba in the morning prayer, a person came and said: The Messenger of God (peace be upon him and his family and companions) had a revelation last night and has been commanded to face the Kaaba, so face it. Their faces were towards Syria, so they turned towards the Kaaba. The story of Quba was in the morning prayer. Al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from al-Bara': When the Messenger of God (peace be upon him and his family and companions) first arrived in Medina, he stayed with his grandfathers (or he said: with his maternal uncles from the Ansar), and he prayed towards Jerusalem for sixteen or seventeen months, and he wished that his qibla be towards the House. He prayed the first prayer (after the change) as the 'Asr prayer, and a group prayed with him. Then someone who had prayed with him left and passed by another mosque where people were bowing. He said: 'I testify by God that I prayed with the Messenger of God (peace be upon him and his family and companions) facing the qibla (Kaaba).' So they turned as they were towards the House. This is another story, and the mosque is not the mosque of Quba, as al-Qastalani explained in his commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari. It occurred in the dawn prayer. Whoever thinks the mosque is the mosque of Quba has erred and forgotten. In summary, the people of the mosque of Quba (or this mosque) acted on a khabar wahid when it opposed a decisive ruling, and they judged that it (the previous ruling) was abrogated. The objection in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that the direction to the Kaaba is established by the Book and is mutawatir does not apply because even if it is from the Book, it was not mutawatir at the time of the report; rather it reached them through a khabar wahid. Understand. And they said: Secondly: He (peace be upon him and his family and companions) used to send individuals to convey rulings, whether new or abrogating. So it is known that abrogation was established by khabar wahid. The answer to both: Khabar wahid may be accompanied by what yields certainty (through surrounding qara'in). This will come in the section on Sunnah. We claim only the non-abrogation of a decisive (ruling) by a report not accompanied (by qara'in). The report of the qibla is of this type because the reporting of this great matter in the presence of the Lawgiver (peace be upon him and his family and companions), and the reporters knew of the Messenger's hope for the change, as in His saying: 'We have seen the turning of your face in the heaven; so We will surely turn you to a qibla which you will like' (Quran 2:144). Similarly for those sent. Reflect on this. You may answer the first argument by saying that the people of Quba and others speculated with the light of insight that the qibla had changed, and their reports coincided with what they speculated, so they acted upon it. Al-Tabarani narrated concerning the change that the Messenger of God (peace be upon him and his family and companions) said: 'Those are men who believed in the unseen.' Thus the Messenger did not consider their reports as (real) khabar wahid and judged that they believed in the unseen, which is a denial of the (normal) path, so it is not proof. In al-Tahrir, the answer to the second argument is: The sending of individuals to convey abrogations of decisive rulings is denied; whoever claims it must provide evidence. Understand. And they said: Thirdly: God says: 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden for an eater to eat except that it be carrion, or blood poured forth, or the flesh of swine' (Quran 6:145). This was abrogated by the prohibition of every fanged beast of prey; that prohibition was established by khabar wahid. To interpret it as specification (takhsis) rather than abrogation is far-fetched because of the temporal distance, as the verse is Meccan while this prohibition was in Medina, and temporal distance in a specifying factor is invalid according to us absolutely, and according to others it is invalid past the time of need. We say: There is no abrogation because the meaning is: 'I do not find (now).' The present tense indicates the present; even if we assume it is possible for it to indicate the future, it is interpreted as present, so there is no removal of the (implied) future prohibition due to the absence of opposition. Even if we accept removal, the non-finding only entails original permissibility. If raising this permissibility (by prohibition) is required, then raising an original permissibility is not abrogation. Reflect. In the margin (al-Hashiya) it is said: The difference between this interpretation (al-taqrir) and the previous one is problematic regarding establishing a legal ruling. The answer is that here there are reports denying the existence of the text, which only entails the non-attachment of the prohibition command. As for the attachment of permissibility, it is not so, unlike the interpretation (al-taqrir) which indicates the attachment of the permissibility command. Understand. Ibn al-Hajib denied the prohibition (of fanged beasts) and thus there is no abrogation; that is because he is Maliki; fanged beasts other than swine are permissible according to him.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi usul dispute on whether a khabar wahid (single report) can abrogate a qati' (definitive) ruling. The author begins by summarizing the position: strength and weakness of conjecture are not considered, except when the report has a strength close to certainty, like the 'well-known' reports in the Hanafi school, which can oppose mutawatir and allow abrogation by addition. Three counterarguments are presented from opponents (likely Shafi'is or others) with Hanafi responses. First argument: The change of qibla at Quba was established by a single caller's report, acting on it under the Prophet's approval shows that a khabar wahid can abrogate a definite ruling (since facing Jerusalem was definite). The Hanafi response: That report was accompanied by qara'in (circumstantial evidence) such as the Prophet's known desire to face the Kaaba, and it occurred in his presence, yielding certainty. Second argument: The Prophet sent individuals to convey abrogations, proving abrogation by khabar wahid. Response: They were sent to convey rulings that were already known to be from the Prophet, and the abrogations were accompanied by qara'in; we only deny abrogation of qati' by an unaccompanied khabar wahid. Third argument: The verse in Surah al-An'am listing prohibited foods was abrogated by the prohibition of fanged beasts, which was established by khabar wahid. Hanafi response: The verse means 'I do not find now' (present tense), so it does not negate future prohibitions; thus there is no abrogation, only specification or a new ruling. The author also notes Ibn al-Hajib's Maliki position that fanged beasts are permissible, so no abrogation occurs. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi insistence on the epistemic distance between zanni and qati' and the requirement that a report be accompanied by qara'in to attain certainty for abrogation.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of tawatur and thus yields zann (conjecture) unless accompanied by qara'in.
قطعي (qat'i): A ruling or text (like mutawatir) that yields certainty (yaqin); cannot be abrogated by a zanni report.
قرينة (qarina): Circumstantial evidence that accompanies a report to elevate it from zann to certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why did the people of Quba act on the single caller's report about the qibla?
A) Because khabar wahid is inherently qat'i when it comes from a trustworthy source.
B) Because the report was accompanied by qara'in that gave it certainty (the Prophet's desire for change and his presence).
C) Because the previous ruling (facing Jerusalem) was not definitively established.
D) Because the Prophet had ordered them to follow any report about the qibla.

Key Takeaway
A khabar wahid cannot abrogate a qati' ruling unless it is accompanied by qara'in that bring it to the level of certainty.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
8 min
Can the Quran Abrogate the Sunnah? Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Mas'ala on permissibility of naskh al-sunnah bi'l-Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on naskh al-sunnah bi'l-Quran and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-arguments using the examples provided in the passage.

Core Idea
The Quran can abrogate the Sunnah: a later Quranic verse can override an earlier Sunnah ruling.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute: can a ruling established by the Sunnah (Prophetic practice) be abrogated by a later Quranic verse? The Hanafi school affirms this, citing two historical examples. The Shafi'i school has reservations, some denying its possibility, others its actual occurrence. Understanding this debate is key to grasping how the two primary sources of Islamic law interact across time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and positions
State the core question: does the Quran have authority to abrogate a ruling from the Sunnah? Identify the Hanafi position (permissible and actual) and the Shafi'i position (two opinions: impossible or possible but not actual).
The Hanafi position is both jawazan (permission) and wuqoo'an (occurrence).
2
Analyze the first example: change of qibla
The direction to Jerusalem was established by the Prophet's practice (Sunnah). The Quranic verse 2:144 commanded facing the Kaaba, thus abrogating the earlier Sunnah. Recognize that this proves actual occurrence.
The objection based on previous law (shari'a of earlier prophets) is rejected because the Prophet faced Jerusalem after hijra, and Christian qibla is East, not Jerusalem.
3
Examine the second example: Ramadan nights
The prohibition of marital relations during Ramadan nights was initially established by Sunnah. Quran 2:187 later permitted it, abrogating that Sunnah. This serves as a second concrete proof.
The verse explicitly mentions 'It is made lawful for you...' indicating abrogation of the prior prohibition.
4
Assess the Shafi'i alternative explanations
Shafi'i scholars propose other possibilities: the abrogator could be a Sunnah reinforced by Quran, or the abrogated ruling could be from an abrogated recitation. The Hanafi response dismisses these as far-fetched and not transmitted.
Accepting such possibilities would undermine the entire discipline of naskh, as anyone could deny a clear abrogator.
5
Understand the methodological principle
The Hanafis rely on the consensus that chronological priority (taqaddum) and posteriority (ta'akhkhur) determine which text is abrogator and which is abrogated. This principle is essential for the science of naskh.
The objection that consensus does not apply here is called 'shay' min al-mukabara' (a form of stubbornness).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: يجوز نسخ السنة بالقرآن) جوازاً وقوعياً، وأصح قولي الشافعي المنع عقلا) كما نقل عن عبد الله بن سعيد (أو سمعاً) كما قال أبو حامد وأبو إسحاق وأبو الطيب الصعلوكي وقيل : ليس بممتنع لا عقلاً ولا سمعاً. لكنه لم يقع قال السبكي: نص الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى لا يدل على أكثر من هذا، وفي كلام المصنف إيماء، إلا أن للشافعي قولين كما قال الآمدي وإمام الحرمين لنا التوجه إلى بيت المقدس ليس في القرآن وقد كان ثابتاً (فكان) ثبوته (بالسنة ونسخ بآية التحويل) فقد ثبت الوقوع وما قيل إن التوجه إلى بيت المقدس لعله كان عملاً بالشريعة السابقة، فإن شرائع من قبلنا كانت حجة، فليس فيه نسخ السنة بالكتاب ساقط، فإن التوجه إلى بيت المقدس كان بعد الهجرة بعدما كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم يتوجه في مكة إلى الكعبة فليس هذا من العمل بالشرع المتقدم أصلاً، وعلى التنزل أن العمل بالشرع المتقدم إنما يكون إذا لم يعلم نسخه أصلاً، وههنا قد انتسخ التوجه إلى بيت المقدس في شريعة عيسى عليه وعلى نبينا وآله وأصحابه السلام فإن قبلة النصارى إلى الشرق (وكذا) لنا (حرمة المباشرة بالنساء في ليالي شهر رمضان، نسخ بقوله تعالى ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ ليْلَةَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّفَثُ إِلَى نِسَا بِكُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۷] الآية مع أن الحرمة ثابتة بالسنة دون الكتاب. وتجويز كون الناسخ (سنة) تعاضدت بالكتاب فصار من قبيل انتساخ السنة بالسنة، فلم يكن من الباب (أو كون المنسوخ كتاباً من منسوخ التلاوة فيكون نسخ الكتاب بالكتاب ولم يكن من الباب فمع بعده جداً لأنه لو كان الأمر كذلك لنقل ولو آحاداً (مندفع بأن معلوم التقدم أو التأخر محكوم عليه بالناسخية أو المنسوخية إجماعاً وقد يقال : الإجماع إنما هو فيما يصلح المؤخر ناسخاً، وههنا لا يصلح لأن الكلام في جواز انتساخ السنة بالكتاب، وهو لا يخلو عن شوب مكابرة، فإنه لو جوّز مثل هذه الاحتمالات لبطل باب الحكم بالنسخ، فإنه يصح يقول في كل نسخ : هذا الناسخ وإن كان معلوم التأخر لا يصلح ناسخاً عندي، فههنا ناسخ آخر
Issue: It is permissible for the Sunnah to be abrogated by the Quran, both in terms of permissibility and actual occurrence. The sounder of Imam al-Shafi'i's two opinions is prohibition, either rationally (as narrated from 'Abdullah ibn Sa'id) or based on transmitted evidence (as stated by Abu Hamid, Abu Ishaq, and Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luqi). It is also said that it is not impossible rationally or by transmitted evidence, but it has not occurred. Al-Subki said: The text of al-Shafi'i (may God have mercy on him) indicates nothing more than this. In the author's words there is a hint, except that al-Shafi'i has two opinions, as al-Amidi and Imam al-Haramayn said. Our (Hanafi) evidence: The direction towards Jerusalem is not in the Quran, yet it was established; so its establishment was by the Sunnah, and it was abrogated by the verse of the change (of qibla). Thus actual occurrence is proven. The objection that the direction towards Jerusalem was perhaps acting upon the previous law (shari'a of previous prophets), for the laws of those before us were proof (but that does not involve abrogation of Sunnah by the Book) is baseless, for the direction towards Jerusalem was after the Hijra, after the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) had faced the Kaaba in Mecca. So this is not from acting upon previous law at all. And even if we concede that acting upon previous law is valid only when its abrogation is not known, here the direction towards Jerusalem was abrogated in the law of Jesus (peace be upon him), for the qibla of Christians is the East. Similarly, our evidence: The prohibition of intercourse with women during the nights of Ramadan was abrogated by His saying: 'It is made lawful for you on the night of the fast to have sexual relations with your wives' (Quran 2:187), even though the prohibition was established by the Sunnah, not the Book. The possibility that the abrogating (verse) is a Sunnah that was reinforced by the Book, so it becomes a case of abrogation of Sunnah by Sunnah, is not relevant. Or the possibility that the abrogated (ruling) was a book from an abrogated recitation, thus abrogation of Book by Book, is not relevant. These possibilities are very far-fetched, because if it were so, it would have been transmitted even as ahad reports. They are repelled by the fact that the known earlier or later (text) is judged to be the abrogator or abrogated by consensus. It might be said: Consensus applies only to what can serve as an abrogator later, and here it cannot because the discussion is about the permissibility of abrogation of Sunnah by the Book. This (objection) is not without a tinge of stubbornness, for if such possibilities are accepted, the entire gate of ruling on abrogation would be invalidated, because one could say in every case of abrogation: This abrogator (though known to be later) is not suitable as an abrogator according to me, so there is another abrogator (i.e., different).
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This is a mas'ala on the permissibility of Sunnah being abrogated by the Quran. The Hanafi position is that it is permissible and has actually occurred. The Shafi'i position has two opinions: the preferred one (as stated) is that it is not permissible, either rationally or based on revealed evidence; some say it is possible but has not occurred. The author provides two examples to prove actual occurrence: first, the direction to Jerusalem was established by Sunnah and abrogated by the Quranic verse of qibla change (2:144). The objection that this was acting on previous law (shari'a of Musa or 'Isa) is rejected because the Prophet faced Jerusalem after Hijra, not during the period of previous law. Also, the Christian qibla is East, so the Jerusalem direction was abrogated in 'Isa's law, so it could not be from that law. Second, the prohibition of intercourse during Ramadan nights was originally from Sunnah (since the Quran did not explicitly prohibit it), and it was abrogated by Quran 2:187 which permits it. The author then rejects alternative explanations like the abrogating being a Sunnah reinforced by Quran, or the abrogated being a Quran of abrogated recitation, by arguing that such speculations are too remote and would undermine the entire science of naskh; if accepted, anyone could deny the abrogating effect of a later text. The consensus is that chronological priority determines abrogator and abrogated.

Key Terms
نسخ السنة بالقرآن (naskh al-sunnah bi'l-quran): Abrogation of a ruling established by the Sunnah (Prophetic practice) by a later Quranic verse.
جوازاً وقوعياً (jawazan wuqoo'iyyan): Both in terms of theoretical permissibility and actual occurrence in history.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, what is the key evidence that the Quran can abrogate the Sunnah?
A) The abrogation of the prohibition of wine.
B) The change of qibla from Jerusalem to the Kaaba.
C) The obligation of fasting in Ramadan.
D) The prohibition of interest.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts that a later Quranic verse can abrogate a ruling originally established by the Sunnah, citing the change of qibla and the permission for Ramadan nights as actual examples.

Naskh — Abrogation

Naskh vs Takhsis: The Case of Predatory Animals
Debate on whether hadith abrogates or specifies Quranic verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between naskh and takhsīs to a case where a later hadith appears to conflict with a Quranic verse, and evaluate the linguistic and temporal arguments used.

Core Idea
A later hadith can specify a Quranic verse without abrogating it when the verse uses present tense and is temporally remote.

At first glance, the prohibition of eating predatory animals by the Prophet ﷺ seems to add a new ruling not mentioned in the Quran. Did this abrogate the Quranic verse that listed only carrion, blood, and pork as forbidden? The Hanafi school says no—it is not abrogation but specification (takhsīs). This lesson unpacks the linguistic and usul reasoning behind that position, which hinges on the present tense of the verse and the temporal gap between the Meccan verse and the Medinan hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى: ﴿قُل لَا أَجِدُ فِي مَا أُوحِيَ إِلَى مُحَرَّمًا عَلَى طَاعِمٍ يَطْعَمُهُ إِلَّا أَن يَكُونَ مَيْتَةً أَوْ دَمًا مَّسْفُوحًا أَوْ لَحْمَ خِنزِيرٍ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٤٥] الآية: نسخ بتحريم كل ذي ناب من السباع من أن التحريم إنما ثبت بخبر الواحد وحمله على التخصيص دون النسخ كما قيل بعيد لكونه متراخياً عنه، فإن الآية مكية، وهذا التحريم كان بالمدينة والتراخي في المخصص باطل عندنا مطلقاً، وعند غيرنا عن وقت الحاجة. قلنا: لا نسخ إذ المعنى لا أجد الآن إذا المضارع ظاهر في الحال ولو تنزل فمحتمل له فيحمل عليه فلا رفع التحريم الاستقبال لعدم المعارضة. ولو سلم الارتفاع فعدم الوجدان إنما يوجب إباحة أصلية. فإن لزم رفع هذه الإباحة فرفع الإباحة الأصلية ليس بنسخ فتدبر. قال في الحاشية: الفرق بين هذا التقرير مشكل في إثبات حكم شرعي والجواب عنه أن ههنا أخباراً بعدم وجدان النص، وهو إنما يوجب عدم تعلق الخطاب بالتحريم وأما تعلقه بالإباحة فكلا، بخلاف التقرير فإنه دال على تعلق الخطاب بالإباحة فافهم. ومنع ابن الحاجب التحريم أي تحريم السباع من البهائم فلا نسخ إنما هو لأنه مالكي، والسباع من البهائم سوى الخنزير مباحة عنده.
Allah Most High said: 'Say: I do not find in what has been revealed to me anything forbidden to a consumer who eats it except that it be carrion, or spilled blood, or flesh of swine' [6:145]. The verse: it is abrogated by the prohibition of every fanged predator – because the prohibition is established by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) – and it is interpreted as specification (takhsīṣ) not abrogation (naskh), as it is said to be far-fetched on account of its being temporally remote from it. For the verse is Meccan, while this prohibition was in Medina, and temporal remoteness in a specifying text is invalid according to us absolutely, and according to others beyond the time of need. We said: There is no abrogation, for the meaning is 'I do not find now' – since the present tense indicates the present state, and even if one concedes otherwise, it is probable, so it is taken accordingly. Thus there is no lifting of the prohibition for the future due to absence of conflict. And if it is conceded that there is lifting, then the non-finding only necessitates original permissibility. If raising this permissibility is necessary, then raising original permissibility is not abrogation, so reflect. The commentator said in the gloss: The difference between this account and that account is problematic in establishing a legal ruling. The answer is that here we have reports of the non-finding of the text, and that only necessitates the non-attachment of address to prohibition; as for its attachment to permissibility, it is not so. Unlike the other account, which indicates the attachment of address to permissibility, so understand. And Ibn al-Hājib denied the prohibition – i.e., the prohibition of predatory animals from beasts – so there is no abrogation; that is because he is a Mālikī, and predatory animals from beasts other than swine are permissible according to him.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about whether a later hadith that prohibits predatory animals abrogates (naskh) or specifies (takhsīṣ) the general Quranic verse in Surah al-An‘am that lists only carrion, blood, and pork as forbidden. The opponents claim the hadith abrogates the verse because it adds a new prohibition. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, the verse is in the present tense ('I do not find'), indicating that at the time of revelation there was no finding of prohibition for predators, but this does not negate future prohibition. Second, temporal remoteness (the verse being Meccan and the hadith Medinan) invalidates the claim of naskh because a later text cannot abrogate an earlier one with a gap in time if it is meant as specification; specification must be contemporaneous. The author also refutes the idea that non-finding of a prohibition implies original permissibility, and distinguishes between reports that merely indicate absence of address versus those that positively indicate permissibility. The gloss clarifies that the first account (the verse) only shows non-attachment of prohibition, not actual permissibility. Finally, Ibn al-Hājib’s rejection is attributed to his being a Mālikī, who permit predatory animals. The ruling is that the prohibition by khabar al-wahid is valid takhsīs of the general verse, not naskh.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation, lifting the former ruling entirely.
تخصيص (takhsīs): Specification of a general text (ʿāmm) by a specific text (khāṣṣ) without abrogating the general meaning.
متراخي (mutarākhī): Temporally remote; a later text that is not contemporaneous with the earlier text.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul argument in this passage, what is the primary reason the prohibition of predatory animals is not considered naskh of the Quranic verse?
A) Because the hadith is mutawātir.
B) Because the verse uses the present tense 'lā ajidu', indicating a current state.
C) Because the prohibition is established by qiyās.
D) Because the verse was abrogated by another Quranic verse.

Key Takeaway
A later hadith can specify a Quranic verse without abrogating it when the verse uses present tense and does not establish a positive legislative ruling.

Naskh — Abrogation

Can the Quran Abrogate the Sunnah? The Hanafi Perspective
Proof and defense of the permissibility of abrogating Sunnah by Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on naskh of Sunnah by Quran, identify the Shafi'i counterargument, and apply the Hanafi response using the concept of 'tabligh'.

Core Idea
The Quran can abrogate the Sunnah because both are divine revelations; the Prophet is a deliverer (muballigh), not a binding explainer.

In this lesson, we examine a classic usul dispute: can a later Quranic verse overrule a ruling established by the Sunnah? The Hanafi school says yes, and offers historical evidence. The Shafi'i school objects on the grounds that the Prophet is an explainer of the Quran. We will dissect the arguments and see how the Hanafis defend their position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi view: naskh of Sunnah by Quran is permissible and has actually occurred. Locate the two historical proofs given in the passage: the change of qibla and the permission of intimacy during Ramadan nights.
Both examples show a Sunnah-established ruling later abrogated by a Quranic verse.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognise the Shafi'i position: the sounder opinion is impossibility by reason (or by revelation). The weaker Shafi'i view admits possibility but denies occurrence. Note the sources cited: 'Abdullah ibn Sa'id, Abu Hamid, Abu Ishaq, al-Su'luki.
Al-Shafi'i reportedly had two opinions; this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i proof: Quran 16:44 describes the Prophet as mubayyin (explainer). Explanation cannot remove what it explains, so Sunnah (the explained) cannot be abrogated by Quran. Also the argument that naskh would cause repulsion (tanfir) by making Allah belie His messenger.
The Shafi'is rely on the literal meaning of 'mubayyin' and psychological effect.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reinterpret 'mubayyin' as 'muballigh' (deliverer) based on context. The Prophet only delivers Allah's commands; if Allah later abrogates a Sunnah by Quran, it is still His command, so no repulsion. The two historical examples are clear evidence of occurrence.
This response preserves the consistency of revelation: both sources are from Allah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if Sunnah can be abrogated by Quran, then rulings like the old qibla are definitively superseded. If not, then such rulings would remain ambiguous or require alternative justification.
This dispute affects how we understand the hierarchy of legal sources in cases of apparent conflict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: يجوز نسخ السنة بالقرآن جوازاً وقوعياً، وأصح قولي الشافعي المنع عقلاً كما نقل عن عبد الله بن سعيد أو سمعاً كما قال أبو حامد وأبو إسحاق وأبو الطيب الصعلوكي وقيل: ليس بممتنع لا عقلاً ولا سمعاً لكنه لم يقع. قال السبكي: نص الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى لا يدل على أكثر من هذا، وفي كلام المصنف إيماء، إلا أن للشافعي قولين كما قال الآمدي وإمام الحرمين. لنا: التوجه إلى بيت المقدس ليس في القرآن وقد كان ثابتاً فكان ثبوته بالسنة ونسخ بآية التحويل فقد ثبت الوقوع. وما قيل إن التوجه إلى بيت المقدس لعله كان عملاً بالشريعة السابقة، فإن شرائع من قبلنا كانت حجة، فليس فيه نسخ السنة بالكتاب ساقط، فإن التوجه إلى بيت المقدس كان بعد الهجرة بعدما كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم يتوجه في مكة إلى الكعبة فليس هذا من العمل بالشرع المتقدم أصلاً، وعلى التنزل أن العمل بالشرع المتقدم إنما يكون إذا لم يعلم نسخه أصلاً، وههنا قد انتسخ التوجه إلى بيت المقدس في شريعة عيسى عليه السلام فإن قبلة النصارى إلى الشرق. وكذا لنا: حرمة المباشرة بالنساء في ليالي شهر رمضان، نسخ بقوله تعالى ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ لَيْلَةَ الصِّيَامِ الرَّفَثُ إِلَى نِسَائِكُمْ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۷] الآية مع أن الحرمة ثابتة بالسنة دون الكتاب. وتجويز كون الناسخ سنة تعاضدت بالكتاب فصار من قبيل انتساخ السنة بالسنة، فلم يكن من الباب، أو كون المنسوخ كتاباً من منسوخ التلاوة فيكون نسخ الكتاب بالكتاب ولم يكن من الباب فمع بعده جداً لأنه لو كان الأمر كذلك لنقل ولو آحاداً. مندفع بأن معلوم التقدم أو التأخر محكوم عليه بالناسخية أو المنسوخية إجماعاً وقد يقال: الإجماع إنما هو فيما يصلح المؤخر ناسخاً، وههنا لا يصلح لأن الكلام في جواز انتساخ السنة بالكتاب، وهو لا يخلو عن شوب مكابرة، فإنه لو جوّز مثل هذه الاحتمالات لبطل باب الحكم بالنسخ، فإنه يصح يقول في كل نسخ: هذا الناسخ وإن كان معلوم التأخر لا يصلح ناسخاً عندي، فههنا ناسخ آخر للمسألة الأصل الأول/ الكتاب هذا معاضد له كيف وقد صح وثبت قطعاً وإجماعاً: أن توجه بيت المقدس كان فرضاً ثم نسخ، ولم ينقل ناسخ سوى القرآن ويحصل بهذا القطع بأن القرآن ناسخ له فافهم، ولا تخبط الشافعية قالوا: أولاً قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَأَنزَلْنَا إِلَيْكَ الذِّكْرَ لِتُبَيِّنَ لِلنَّاسِ مَا نُزِّلَ إِلَيْهِمْ﴾ [النحل: ٤٤] . هو مبين بالكسر، أي ما به البيان لكل ما نزل إليهم، ومنه السنة والبيان لا يرفع مبينه بالفتح وسقط ما قال ميرزاجان أن غاية ما لزم منه أنه مبين للقرآن، فلا يلزم منه إلا عدم انتساخ القرآن بكلامه لا عدم انتساخ كلامه بما هو ناقل من الله تعالى، فهذا الوجه وجه الثانية، وإيراده هنا تحريف الكلم عن مواضعه، وذلك لأنه قد لزم منه أنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم مبين بالقرآن فهو البيان :نعم :ينقض بانتساخ القرآن بالقرآن، فإنه أيضاً مما نزل إليهم فيكون بياناً فلا نسخ به فتأمل فيه. قلنا: أولاً البيان ههنا بمعنى التبليغ، والمعنى وأنزلنا إليك الكتاب لتبلغ الناس ما نزل إليهم، فليس هو ببيان للحكم حتى لا يكون رافعاً. وثانياً لو سلم أن البيان بيان الحكم فإنما لا يرفع السنة بمبينة بالكسر من القرآن لا بغيره بل يجوز أن تكون مبينة بآية منسوخة بأخرى. وقالوا ثانياً فيه أي في نسخ الكتاب السنة تنفير للناس أن الله يكذب رسوله ويرفع حكمه. قلنا: لا نسلم أن فيه تنفيراً، كيف وإذا علم أنه مبلغ فقط لا مخترع من عند نفسه فلا نفرة، لأن ما جرى على لسانه الشريف حكم الله تعالى فلا وهم للنفرة فافهم.
Issue: It is permissible to abrogate the Sunnah by the Quran, permissibly and actually. The sounder of al-Shafi'i's two opinions is impossibility by reason, as transmitted from 'Abdullah ibn Sa'id, or by revelation, as Abu Hamid, Abu Ishaq, and Abu al-Tayyib al-Su'luki said. And it is said: It is not impossible by reason or revelation, but it has not occurred. al-Subki said: al-Shafi'i's text does not indicate more than this, and in the author's words there is an allusion, except that al-Shafi'i has two opinions as al-Amidi and Imam al-Haramayn said. Our proof: Facing Bayt al-Maqdis is not in the Quran, yet it was established; hence its establishment was by the Sunnah, and it was abrogated by the verse of turning (al-tahwil), so occurrence is established. And what is said that facing Bayt al-Maqdis was perhaps acting on the previous law, for the laws of those before us were authoritative, so there is no abrogation of Sunnah by the Book, is invalid. For facing Bayt al-Maqdis was after the Hijra, after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and Companions) and his Companions used to face the Ka'bah in Mecca, so this is not acting on the previous law at all. And even if conceding, acting on the previous law is only when its abrogation is not known at all, whereas here facing Bayt al-Maqdis had been abrogated in the law of Jesus (peace be on him), for the Christians' qibla is to the east. Similarly, our proof: The prohibition of intercourse with women on the nights of Ramadan was abrogated by Allah's saying: 'Permitted to you on the night of fasting is approach to your wives' [2:187], whereas the prohibition was established by the Sunnah, not the Book. And the suggestion that the abrogator is a Sunnah that is reinforced by the Book, so it becomes a case of abrogation of Sunnah by Sunnah, and thus not our issue, or that the abrogated is a Book of abrogated recitation, so it becomes abrogation of Book by Book, and thus not our issue, besides being far-fetched because if it were so, it would have been transmitted even if individually, is repelled by: The known earlier or later is ruled as abrogating or abrogated by consensus. And it may be said: Consensus is only regarding what qualifies as a later abrogator, and here it does not qualify, because the discussion is about the permissibility of abrogating Sunnah by the Book, and this is not free from a tinge of obstinacy, for if such probabilities were allowed, the door of ruling on abrogation would be invalidated, for one could say in every case of abrogation: This abrogator, even if known to be later, does not qualify as an abrogator to me, so here is another abrogator for the issue. The first principle: The Book is a support for it; how? And it has been soundly established by definitive proof and consensus that facing Bayt al-Maqdis was an obligation then abrogated, and no abrogator besides the Quran has been transmitted. By this it is definitively concluded that the Quran is its abrogator, so understand. And do not be confused by the Shafi'is. They said: First, Allah said: 'And We sent down to you the Reminder that you may explain to the people what has been sent down to them' [16:44]. He is the explainer (mubayyin) in the sense of 'what has the explanation', i.e., that by which every thing sent down to them is explained, and from it is the Sunnah. And the explanation does not remove what is explained. And what Mirzājān said – that the most that follows is that he is explainer of the Quran, so only the impossibility of abrogating the Quran by his words follows, not the impossibility of abrogating his words by what is transmitted from Allah – this is the second aspect, and citing it here is twisting words from their places, because it follows from it that he (peace be upon him) is explainer by the Quran, so he is the explanation. Yes, it is refuted by the abrogation of the Quran by the Quran, for it too is among what was sent down to them, so it would be an explanation, and thus no abrogation by it – so reflect on it. We said: First, 'explanation' here means 'delivery' (tabligh); the meaning is: We sent down to you the Book that you may deliver to the people what was sent down to them. So it is not an explanation of the ruling such that it would not be a remover. Second, even if it is conceded that the explanation is explanation of the ruling, then it does not remove the Sunnah when it is the explained (mubayyan) by the Quran, not by other [i.e., the Sunnah cannot be abrogated by a Quranic verse if that verse is explanation of the Sunnah? Actually the text is tricky]. They said second: In it i.e., in abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah, there is repulsion of people that Allah belies His messenger and removes his ruling. We said: We do not concede that there is repulsion; how? When it is known that he is only a deliverer, not an innovator from himself, so there is no repulsion, because what proceeds on his noble tongue is the ruling of Allah, so there is no illusion of repulsion, so understand.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi defense of the permissibility of abrogating Sunnah (Prophetic tradition) by the Quran. The issue is one of usul: can a later Quranic verse supersede a ruling established by hadith? The Shafi'i position (stronger view) is that it is impossible, either rationally or scripturally. The Hanafis give two historical proofs: (1) the change of qibla from Jerusalem to the Ka'ba – the obligation to face Jerusalem was established by Sunnah (as it is not mentioned in the Quran), yet it was abrogated by the Quranic verse commanding the new qibla (Q. 2:144). The objection that this might be acting on previous revelation is refuted because it was practiced after the Hijra while the Prophet was already in Mecca facing the Ka'ba, and also the earlier law of Jesus had already abrogated facing Jerusalem. (2) The prohibition of marital intimacy on Ramadan nights was established by Sunnah (since no verse initially prohibited it), yet it was abrogated by Q. 2:187 which permits it. The passage also rebuts the Shafi'i argument that the Prophet is an explainer (mubayyin) of the Quran, which they claim would prevent abrogation of his Sunnah by the Quran because explanation cannot remove what it explains. The Hanafi response is that 'explanation' here means 'delivery' (tabligh), not a binding explanation that prevents abrogation. Additionally, the claim that abrogation of Sunnah by Quran would cause repulsion (tanfir) is rejected because the Prophet is merely a deliverer of Allah's commands; if Allah abrogates a Sunnah by Quran, it is still His command, so no repulsion.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation.
مبين (mubayyin): Explainer: the Prophet is described as explaining the Quran.
تبليغ (tablīgh): Delivery: the Prophet's role is to convey the message of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which historical event is used as proof that Sunnah can be abrogated by the Quran?
A) The prohibition of wine.
B) The change of qibla from Jerusalem to the Ka'ba.
C) The obligation of fasting Ramadan.
D) The punishment for adultery.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms the permissibility and occurrence of naskh of Sunnah by Quran, proven by the change of qibla and the Ramadan intimacy verse.

Naskh — Abrogation

Can Sunnah Abrogate Quran? — The Hanafi Usul Position
Proof that Sunnah can abrogate Quran, with refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on naskh of Quran by Sunnah, cite the primary dalil (hadith 'No will for an heir'), and refute the Shafi'i objection using usul principles.

Core Idea
Sunnah can abrogate Quran because both are divine revelation differing only in wording.

This passage tackles a foundational usul dispute: can an ahad hadith abrogate a Quranic verse? The Hanafi school says yes, and the hadith 'No will for an heir' (la wasiyyata li-warith) is a concrete example. The Shafi'i school denies this absolutely. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rational and textual proof, and examines an internal Hanafi counter-claim that the abrogator was actually another verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
State the positions: Hanafi (permissible and actual) vs. Shafi'i (impossible). Understand that the Shafi'i view is based on the Quran's higher authority.
2
Analyze the Hanafi rational argument
Both Quran and Sunnah are divine rulings; they differ only in wording (nazm). Therefore, one can lift (raf') the other's ruling. This is a logical possibility.
The author calls denial of this 'obstinacy' (mukabarah).
3
Examine the textual proof: hadith vs. verse
The hadith 'No will for an heir' is cited as abrogating Q. 2:180 which commanded a will for parents and close relatives (who are heirs). Identify that this is a case of naskh of Quran by Sunnah.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear and prohibitive.
4
Evaluate the internal Hanafi counter-argument
Some Hanafis (al-Jassas, Fakhr al-Islam) argued that the abrogator is the inheritance verse (4:11), not the hadith. Understand their reasoning: the inheritance verse mentions an indefinite will, implying the definite will was abrogated.
The author dismisses this as weak (marjuh) because inheritance is after the will.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that the hadith is the abrogator, establishing naskh of Quran by Sunnah. The counter-claim is a minority opinion.
This is the dominant position in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: يجوز نسخ الكتاب بالسنة خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله تعالى قطعاً فإن له قولاً واحداً فيه، لا كما يوهم المنهاج أن فيه أيضاً له قولين. لنا: هذا النسخ ممكن لذاته فإنه إذا نظرنا إلى مفهومه لا يأبى الوقوع وليس ممتنعاً بالغير لأن الأصل عدمه لكن أصحاب الشافعي لا يقنعون عليه بل يمنعون الإمكان، فإن رب شيء لا يمنعه العقل ويظهر استحالته، ولعله يشبه المكابرة، وتفصيل الدليل أن الكتاب لا يزيد على السنة إلا بالنظم، وأما الحكم فحكم كل منهما حكم الله تعالى، فلا يستحيل أن يرفع أحدهما الآخر، وكذا لا يستحيل أن يبين أحدهما الآخر، وإنكاره مكابرة. واستدل بأن قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: لا وصية لوارث نسخ الوصية للوالدين والأقربين الثابت بقوله تعالى {كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ إِن تَرَكَ خَيْرًا الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالْأَقْرَبِينَ} [البقرة: ١٨٠] وقول جماعة منهم الشيخ أبو بكر الجصاص والإمام فخر الإسلام وتبعهما كثير منهم صدر الشريعة ليس الناسخ الحديث بل الناسخ آية المواريث فليس من الباب. مرجوح فإنها أي آية المواريث لا تعارضه أي وجوب الوصية للأقرباء لأن الميراث بعد الوصية فيجوز أن تكون من والثلث والميراث في الباقي، وفي «الحاشية» وبه قال الفقيه أبو الليث: اعلم أن الإمام فخر الإسلام أثبت المعارضة والنسخ بوجهين وقال بيانه أنه قال: مِن بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصَى بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ [النساء: ١١] فرتب الميراث على وصية منكرة والوصية الأولى كانت معهودة، فلو كانت تلك الوصية باقية مع الميراث ثم نسخت بالسنة لوجب ترتبه على المعهودة، فصار الإطلاق نسخاً للقيد كما يكون القيد نسخاً للإطلاق انتهت كلماته الشريفة واعترض الشيخ الهداد في شرحه.
Issue: It is permissible to abrogate the Book by the Sunnah, contrary to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), definitively; for he has one opinion on it, not as the Minhaj suggests that he also has two opinions. Our proof: This abrogation is possible in itself, for when we look at its concept, it does not reject occurrence, and it is not impossible due to an external factor, because the original is absence (of impossibility). However, al-Shafi'i's followers are not satisfied with this, but they deny possibility, for many a thing that reason does not prevent appears impossible to them, and it perhaps resembles obstinacy. The detailed proof is that the Book does not surpass the Sunnah except in wording; as for the ruling, each of their rulings is the ruling of Allah, so it is not impossible for one to lift the other, and likewise it is not impossible for one to explain the other, and its denial is obstinate. And they argued using his saying (peace be upon him and his family and Companions): 'There is no will for an heir.' It abrogates the will for parents and close relatives established by His saying: 'Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves behind wealth, is to make a will for parents and close relatives' [2:180]. And a group, among them Shaykh Abu Bakr al-Jassas and Imam Fakhr al-Islam, followed by many including Sadr al-Shari'ah, said: The abrogator is not the hadith, rather the abrogator is the verse of inheritance, so it is not of this issue. But this is weak, for the verse of inheritance does not contradict the obligation of will for relatives, because inheritance comes after the will, so it is possible that [the will] be from one-third and the inheritance from the remainder. And in the gloss, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: Know that Imam Fakhr al-Islam established contradiction and abrogation in two ways, and said its explanation is that He said: 'from after a will he bequeaths or a debt' [4:11]. He arranged inheritance on an indefinite will, while the first will was definite. So if that will remained with inheritance and then was abrogated by the Sunnah, it would be necessary to arrange it on the definite, so the indefinite became an abrogation of the definite just as a definite can abrogate an indefinite. End of his noble words. And Shaykh al-Haddad objected in his commentary.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi assertion that Sunnah can abrogate the Quran. The Shafi'i position is that this is impossible. The Hanafi rational argument: both Quran and Sunnah are divine revelation; they differ only in wording, not in legal authority, so one can abrogate the other. The main proof presented is the hadith 'No will for an heir' which abrogated the Quranic verse (2:180) that obligated a will for parents and relatives. Some Hanafi scholars (like al-Jassas, Fakhr al-Islam) claimed that the abrogator is actually the inheritance verses (e.g., 4:11), not the hadith, thus keeping the issue within naskh of Quran by Quran. But the majority Hanafi position rejects this because the inheritance verses do not conflict with the will verse; they assign shares after the will, so the will obligation remains. However, Fakhr al-Islam argued that the inheritance verse mentions an indefinite will (nekara) while the first verse spoke of a definite will, and by the law of inheritance imposing shares, the specific obligation of will was implicitly abrogated. The gloss reports that Shaykh al-Haddad objected to this reasoning. The taken position is that the hadith is the abrogator, proving naskh of Quran by Sunnah.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later text.
وصية (wasiyya): A will or bequest made by a person before death.
وارث (wārith): An heir who inherits under Islamic law.
مرجوح (marjuh): A weaker or outweighed opinion in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith is cited as evidence that the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran?
A) 'The prayer is the pillar of religion.'
B) 'There is no will for an heir.'
C) 'Actions are judged by intentions.'
D) 'He who innovates in this matter is rejected.'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Sunnah can abrogate Quran, as exemplified by the hadith 'No will for an heir' abrogating Q. 2:180, and this position is established through rational and textual arguments.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
15 min
Permissibility of Abrogating the Quran by the Sunnah
Hanafi defense of naskh al-kitab bi al-sunnah with detailed refutation of Shafi'i objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi proof for naskh al-kitab bi al-sunnah and refute the Shafi'i counterarguments using the textual and rational arguments presented in this passage.

Core Idea
The Quran and Sunnah share the same divine ruling (hukm); therefore, the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran.

One of the most debated issues in usul al-fiqh is whether the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran. The Hanafi school affirms this possibility, while the Shafi'i school denies it. This passage presents the Hanafi case, grounded in both rational argument and textual example. You will follow the logical flow of the dispute, from the Shafi'i objections based on Quran 16:44 and the claim of 'repulsion', to the Hanafi response, concluding with the concrete example of the hadith 'No bequest to an heir' abrogating the bequest verse (2:180).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue and schools' positions
Read the first part of the passage to determine the exact point of disagreement: does the Sunnah have authority to abrogate a Quranic ruling? Note the Hanafi stance (permissible) and the Shafi'i stance (not permissible).
The passage states the Shafi'i view is a single opinion, not two as some suggest.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i arguments and the Hanafi response
Two Shafi'i arguments are presented: (1) Quran 16:44 says the Prophet explains (yubayyin) the Quran, and explanation cannot abrogate. (2) Abrogation would cause repulsion (tanfir) among people. The Hanafi response reinterprets 'bayan' as 'tabligh' (delivery) and denies repulsion by affirming the Prophet is merely a deliverer.
Focus on the linguistic analysis of 'bayan' and how the Hanafis shift the meaning to avoid the implication.
3
Examine the rational proof for possibility
The Hanafi proof is that the Quran and Sunnah differ only in wording (nazm); their rulings (hukm) are both divine. Hence, one can abrogate the other. This is a philosophical argument based on the nature of revelation.
The text calls denial of this 'obstinacy' (mukabarah).
4
Work through the bequest example as an actual case
The hadith 'لا وصية لوارث' (No bequest to an heir) is presented as an actual instance of naskh. Understand how it abrogates the obligation in Quran 2:180. Some Hanafi scholars argue the abrogator is actually the inheritance verses (4:11), but the author defends the hadith as the direct abrogator.
Follow the detailed discussion of the relationship between the two verses and how the author rebuts objections from Shaykh al-Haddad.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Conclude by understanding the practical consequence: for Hanafis, the obligation to bequeath to heirs is removed; for Shafi'is, it remains but is limited by other rules. This illustrates how the usul dispute affects actual fiqh rulings.
The passage ends with a report from Ibn Abbas supporting abrogation by inheritance verses, but the author considers that as corroboration.

For the issue [of naskh]: The first principle [from] the Book supports this. How, when it has been established and proven definitively and by consensus that facing Bayt al-Maqdis was obligatory then abrogated, and no abrogator was transmitted except the Quran, and by this it is definitively established that the Quran abrogated it. So understand, and do not be confused by the Shafi'is who said: First, Allah said: 'And We revealed to you the Reminder that you may make clear to the people what was revealed to them' (16:44). It is 'mubayyin' (with kasra), meaning that by which explanation is made for everything revealed to them, and from this is the Sunnah. And 'al-bayan' (the explanation) does not remove [the explained]. [The word] 'mubayyan' is with fatha. And what Mirzajan said that the utmost entailed is that he is an explainer of the Quran, so nothing follows except the non-abrogation of the Quran by his speech, not the non-abrogation of his speech by what is transmitted from Allah. So this is the second aspect, and its mention here is distortion of words from their places. Because it entails that he (peace be upon him) is explained by the Quran, so he is the explanation. Yes, it is refuted by the abrogation of the Quran by the Quran, for that too is among what was revealed to them, so it would be an explanation, so no abrogation by it. Reflect on it. (We said) First, 'al-bayan' here means 'tabligh' (delivery). The meaning is: We revealed the Book to you so that you may deliver to the people what was revealed to them. So it is not an explanation of the ruling such that it would not be removing. Second, even if it is granted that 'bayan' is explanation of the ruling, it does not remove the Sunnah when it is explained (with kasra) by the Quran, not by other than it. Rather, it is permissible that it be explained by a verse that is abrogated by another. And they said, Second: In this (i.e., abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah) there is repulsion for people [thinking] that Allah lies to His messenger and removes His ruling. (We said) We do not accept that there is repulsion in it. How, when it is known that it implies that he is only a deliverer, not an innovator from himself. So no repulsion, because what proceeds from his noble tongue is the ruling of Allah, so there is no illusion of repulsion. So understand. Issue: It is permissible to abrogate the Book by the Sunnah, contrary to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) definitively, for he has a single opinion on it, not as al-Minhaj implies that he has two opinions. (Our proof) this abrogation is possible in itself, because when we look at its concept, it does not preclude occurrence. And it is not impossible due to an external factor because the default is its absence. But the followers of al-Shafi'i are not satisfied with this; rather they deny its possibility. Indeed, some things are not prevented by reason yet appear impossible, and perhaps it resembles obstinacy. The detail of the proof is that the Book does not exceed the Sunnah except in wording (nazm). As for the ruling, the ruling of each is the ruling of Allah, so it is not impossible for one to remove the other, nor for one to explain the other. Denying it is obstinacy. And they argued by his saying (peace be upon him): 'No bequest to an heir' which abrogated the bequest to parents and close relatives established by His saying: 'Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, [is] the bequest to parents and close relatives' (2:180). And the statement of a group, including Shaykh Abu Bakr al-Jassas and Imam Fakhr al-Islam, followed by many including Sadr al-Shari'ah, that the abrogator is not the hadith; rather the abrogator is the verse of inheritance, so it is not from the [present] topic. [This opinion] is weak because it [the verse of inheritance] does not contradict it [the obligation of bequest to relatives] because inheritance comes after bequest, so it is possible that [the bequest] be from and inheritance in the remainder. And in al-Hashiyah: Abu al-Layth said: Know that Imam Fakhr al-Islam established contradiction and abrogation in two ways. He said in its explanation: He said: 'after a bequest [made] or debt' (4:11), thus he made inheritance conditional upon an indefinite bequest, while the first bequest was definite. If that bequest remained with inheritance and then was abrogated by the Sunnah, it would have to be conditional upon the definite one. Thus the absolute [expression] became an abrogation of the restricted, just as restriction abrogates the absolute. His noble words ended. Shaykh al-Haddad objected in his commentary saying: The meaning is not 'after an absolute bequest' i.e., any bequest, such that it would entail establishing inheritance after a single bequest without executing the bequest to parents and relatives. Rather, the meaning is that inheritance comes after every bequest among bequests, as required by the qualified indefinite, and this includes the obligatory bequest. So it does not contradict the ruling of the obligatory bequest. And this servant says, while acknowledging the lowliness of objecting to such men, that the ruling of the verse of bequest is its obligation at death and leaving wealth. When the bequest of wealth to an heir becomes obligatory, no room remains for bequest to a non-heir. The verse of inheritance indicates the necessity of inheritance after execution of bequests issued by the deceased, so from it follows legislation of absolute bequest without obligation. No doubt this absoluteness removes the obligation entirely, just as restriction removes absoluteness. This is very obvious. And it has been established in the commentary of al-Badi' that the bequest mentioned here is indefinite while there it is definite, and when a thing is repeated indefinitely, the second is other than the first. So the verse of inheritance indicates that inheritance is prescribed after the supererogatory bequest, which contradicts the obligation of bequest because it invalidates inheritance, so abrogation necessarily follows. Shaykh al-Haddad objected first that the ordering of inheritance after the non-obligatory bequest is established by textual indication, so there is no contradiction. Second, the distinctness of the second from the first is not universal; rather it may fail in many places, so it does not nullify the established obligation of bequest. And this servant, may Allah forgive him, says: This has no merit, because the default in speech is distinctness unless there is a counter-indication, and there is none, so it is taken accordingly. If the possibility of metaphorical [interpretation] were to hinder abrogation, abrogation would be entirely invalidated. And when it is established, the ordering of inheritance after the non-obligatory bequest is established, and the wealth becomes occupied with inheritance, thus nullifying another disposal besides it and besides the supererogatory bequest, so it definitively removes the obligatory bequest. Understand, for it is subtle. And he explained the second way by saying: Its explanation is that Allah entrusted the making of bequests to relatives to the servants by His saying: 'Bequest to parents and close relatives with kindness' (2:180). Then He Himself undertook the explanation of that right and confined it to the limits of its necessary consequence, and by it that same right was established. So it shifted from the mode of bequest to the mode of inheritance. And to this He alluded by His saying: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children' (4:11), i.e., that which He entrusted to you He Himself undertook when you were unable to determine its measures. Do you not see His saying: 'You do not know which of them is nearer to you in benefit, an obligation from Allah' (4:11). And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, Allah has given every rightful person his right, so no bequest to an heir' i.e., by this prescription He abrogated the first ruling. His noble words ended. Shaykh al-Haddad objected that the verse is not decisive (muhkam) in this meaning; rather it is possible that the meaning is: Allah instructs you regarding the division of the estate in this manner, and He did not entrust you with division alone, because you do not know which of them is nearer in benefit to you. So this bequest is not that which He entrusted to them; rather what was entrusted to them remains as it was. In that case, there is no contradiction and no abrogation. And you are aware that rulings are not conditional upon decisiveness in abrogation; rather apparentness (zuhur) is sufficient. How so? The verse of bequest is not decisive (muhkam) in establishing obligation of bequest due to the possibility of another meaning. As it was commanded to be apparent (zahir) in establishing obligation of bequest, there is no obstruction in its abrogation by another apparent [text]. And know that al-Bukhari and al-Bayhaqi narrated from Ibn 'Abbas: 'The wealth was for the child, and the bequest for parents and close relatives. Then Allah abrogated that as He willed, so He made for the male the share of two females, and for each of them the sixth with the child, and for the wife the eighth and the quarter, and for the husband the half and the quarter.' And the statement of a Companion regarding reports about abrogation will come from...
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of abrogating a Quranic ruling by a Sunnah (hadith), a contested issue between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi position, as presented here, is that such abrogation is possible and has occurred. The author begins by citing the case of the change of the qibla from Jerusalem to Mecca as evidence that the Quran abrogated itself, implying that the Sunnah could also abrogate the Quran. The Shafi'i argument using the verse 'we revealed the Reminder that you may explain' (16:44) is refuted by interpreting 'bayan' as 'tabligh' (delivery), not legal explanation, and that even if it were explanation, it does not prevent the Sunnah from being abrogated by the Quran or vice versa. The second Shafi'i argument about 'repulsion' (tanfir) is dismissed because the Prophet is merely a deliverer of divine rulings. The core Hanafi proof is logical: both the Quran and Sunnah share the same divine source in terms of the ruling (hukm); they differ only in wording (nazm), so one can abrogate the other. The main example is the abrogation of the obligatory bequest to parents and close relatives (2:180) by the hadith 'No bequest to an heir'. Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Jassas, Fakhr al-Islam) argued that the abrogator is actually the inheritance verses (4:11) rather than the hadith, but the author sides with the majority view that the hadith is the abrogator. A detailed discussion follows on the interpretation of 'after a bequest' (4:11), showing that the inheritance verses refer to a supererogatory bequest, not the obligatory one, thus conflicting with and abrogating the obligatory bequest. Objections by al-Haddad are rebutted by affirming the default distinctness of terms and the sufficiency of apparent (zahir) texts for abrogation. The passage ends with a narration from Ibn Abbas confirming that the abrogation occurred through the inheritance verses, though the exact source of the narration is cut off. This entire discussion exemplifies the Hanafi methodology of using rational and textual arguments to defend a foundational usul principle.

Key Terms
نَسْخ (naskh): Abrogation: removal of a legal ruling by a later divine address.
بَيَان (bayan): In this passage, initially claimed by Shafi'is as 'explanation' that cannot abrogate, but Hanafis reinterpret as 'tabligh' (delivery).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the primary proof for the permissibility of abrogating the Quran by the Sunnah?
A) The Quran itself states that the Sunnah is an independent source of law.
B) The Quran and Sunnah are both divine in terms of ruling (hukm), differing only in wording (nazm), making one capable of abrogating the other.
C) The consensus of the Companions that the Sunnah can abrogate the Quran.
D) The hadith 'No bequest to an heir' explicitly abrogates the bequest verse.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits naskh al-kitab bi al-sunnah because the ruling (hukm) of both Quran and Sunnah is divine; the difference is only in wording, so abrogation is rationally possible and factually occurred in the case of bequests to heirs.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
8 min
How the Inheritance Verses Abrogate the Obligatory Will
Analyzing conflict between wasiyyah and inheritance verses leading to naskh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi linguistic argument that the inheritance verses refer to a supererogatory will and thereby abrogate the obligation of wasiyyah for heirs.

Core Idea
The inheritance verses prescribe shares after a will that is supererogatory, not obligatory, thus abrogating the earlier obligation.

The apparent conflict between the verse obligating wasiyyah for parents and relatives (2:180) and the inheritance verses (4:11-12) that fix shares for heirs is resolved by recognizing that the inheritance verses speak of a will that is not obligatory. This lesson walks through the key linguistic and contextual arguments that lead to the conclusion of naskh (abrogation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting texts
Locate Quran 2:180 (obligatory will for parents and relatives) and Quran 4:11-12 (fixed inheritance shares). Note the apparent contradiction: if a will is obligatory for heirs, it would consume the inheritance before the shares are applied.
The conflict is only apparent if the will is obligatory for heirs. If the will is supererogatory, no conflict arises.
2
Analyze the indefinite repetition argument
The inheritance verses mention 'after a will' without specifying the type. In Arabic, an indefinite noun repeated as indefinite indicates a different entity. So the will in the inheritance verses is not the same obligatory will but a supererogatory one.
This linguistic principle is key: 'wasīyah' in 2:180 is definite (al-wasīyah), while in 4:11 it is indefinite (wasīyatin), implying a different kind of will.
3
Trace the logical implication
If the will is supererogatory, then inheritance shares follow it. If the will were obligatory, it would preoccupy the wealth and block the shares. Thus, the obligatory nature must have been abrogated.
This reasoning is presented as 'this absolute lifts obligation entirely, just as restriction lifts absoluteness'.
4
Consider the objection and response
Shaykh al-Haddad objects that indefinite repetition does not always imply difference; there are exceptions. The Hanafi response is that the default is difference unless a diverting factor exists, and here there is none.
The response relies on the principle of 'the reality of speech is difference' (ḥaqīqat al-kalām al-mughāyara).
5
Confirm the evidence from Ibn Abbas
Ibn Abbas reported that the practice was to will for parents/relatives until the inheritance verses abrogated that ruling. This Companion statement supports the naskh.
This is cited as evidence, but not the primary proof.

سيجي من الأصل الأول/ الكتاب حجة، فلا بد من حمل آية الميراث على أحد الوجوه المذكورة، ولو جعل قوله تعالى : لِلرِّجَالِ نَصِيبٌ مِّمَّا تَرَكَ الْوَالِدَانِ وَالْأَقْرَبُونَ ﴾ [النساء : ٧] ناسخاً كما روي الخبر، وهذا غير واف لأن الحنفية لا يجوزون نسخ المقطوع بالخبر المشهور إلا النسخ بزيادة (لكن) (قال الإمام أبو زيد) القاضي (لم يوجد في كتاب الله ما ينسخ بالسنة إلا من طريق الزيادة فعلى هذا لا يصح التزام انتساخ آية الوصية بهذا الخبر ولو بلغ أحد القطع (قيل) في تقرير الكلام الأوجه أن يقال : الإجماع على الحكم المتأخر دليل وجود الناسخ لأن الإجماع لا يكون خطأ، فلا بد من انتساخ الحكم المتقدم وههنا قد أجمع
