Why Consensus Cannot Abrogate: The Need for Revelation
Hanafi proof that naskh requires knowledge of ruling duration, which only revelation provides

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that ijma cannot abrogate because naskh requires knowledge of ruling duration from revelation, and evaluate the opposing view by identifying the four objections and Hanafi responses.

Core Idea
Ijma cannot abrogate; only revelation knows a ruling's term.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut, the author defends the Hanafi position that consensus (ijma) cannot serve as an abrogator (nasikh). The key insight is that abrogation requires knowledge of a ruling's duration, which is known only through divine revelation (wahi), not human opinion. The text then engages with and refutes objections from opponents who allow naskh by ijma.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi claim
Identify the central argument: abrogation requires knowing the lifespan of a ruling, which only revelation can provide. The author states: 'لا مدخل للرأي في انتهاء مدة الحكم'.
2
Understand the opponent's objection
The opponent argues that ijma could be based on a text, so the text is the real abrogator, or ijma could know the term via inspiration. The text presents four objections.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
For each objection, explain the Hanafi rebuttal: (1) the text is the abrogator, ijma is only revealer; (2) unknown timing doesn't negate possibility; (3) abrogation without error; (4) ahad vs mutawatir.
4
Synthesize the final position
Conclude that ijma cannot abrogate; if based on a text, the text abrogates; if based on inspiration, it cannot contradict Sharia. The author says: 'فالحق في استدلال ما مر من أن الإجماع الناسخ إن كان عن مستند فهو ثابت من الزمان الشريف، فإذن الناسخ هو.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني وهو أن الإجماع لا يكون ناسخاً (فللعنيفة أنه لا مدخل للرأي في انتهاء مدة الحكم في علمه تعالى بل يعرف ( بالوحي) يعني أن النسخ ليس إلا رفع الحكم بعد وجوده أو إبانة مدة الحكم، وعلى التقديرين لا شك أنه لا بد للنسخ من معرفة عمر الحكم ولا مدخل للرأي فيه، فأهل الإجماع لا يعرفونه فلا ينسخونه، بل إنما يعرف بالوحي فهو الناسخ حقيقة (أقول) مسلم أن الرأي المحض لا يعرف مدة الحكم لكن لا يلزم منه عدم ناسخية الإجماع، بل لعل المستند معرف لهم فبعد معرفة مدة الحكم بالمستند يحكمون بالحكم المخالف للأول ويعرفونه (فافهم وهذا ليس بشيء، لأن هذا المستند إما رأي محض أو وحي، والأول لا يصلح معرفاً، وعلى الثاني هو الناسخ دون الإجماع، وقد يمنع عدم مدخلية الآراء في معرفة مدة الحكم، ويقال : إنما لا يعرف مدد أحكام الوحي دون أحكام الإجماع، وجوابه أنه لا يدخل للرأي المحض في معرفة الأحكام، بل لا بد من مستند شرعي، والقياس منه لا يفيد معرفة المدة، والنص هو الناسخ فتدبر ، ثم يتوجه إليه أنه يجوز أن يكون الإجماع بلا مستند بل بإلهام تعالى لأهل الإجماع، فيجوز أن يلهموا مدة الحكم وقد عرفت ما يفي لدفع هذا ( ولغيرهم) أي لغير الحنفية في هذا المطلب أنه إن كان الإجماع الناسخ (عن نص فهو الناسخ) حقيقة دون الإجماع والإجماع كاشف عن وجود هذا النص (وإلا) يكن الإجماع الناسخ عن نص، بل عن قياس أو إلهام لو جوّز (فإن كان الأول المنسوخ نصاً كان أو إجماعاً قطعياً، فالإجماع) الناسخ (خطأ) لأن خلاف القاطع خطأ وإن كان الأول المنسوخ (ظنياً لم يبق مع الإجماع لزوال شرط العمل به (وهو الرجحان بالقطع الذي هو الإجماع، وإذا لم يبق لم يعارض الإجماع إياه فلا ينسخه (وفيه) أوّلاً (أن كون النسخ بالنص دونه) كما قلتم في تلك الشق الأول ( يبطل حجيته لأنه حينئذ النص هو (الحجة دون الإجماع، فحينئذ لا تصح المقدمة. والجواب عنه ظاهر، لأن المدعي عدم إثباته للحكم، بل إنه حجة بمعنى أنه كاشف، وإنما المثبت النص المستند لكننا لا ننتظر في معرفة الحكم المجمع عليه إلى معرفة المستند معه كاشف عن الأصل الأول/ الكتاب لكونه قاطعاً في إبانة الحكم فتأمل (و) فيه ثانياً (أنه ربما كان النص) المستند (غير معلوم التأخر فلا يصلح ناسخاً بخلاف الإجماع) فإنه معلوم التأخر ، فحينئذ لا نسلم أنه إن كان عن نص فهو الناسخ والجواب عنه ظاهر، فإن عدم العلم بالتأخر إنما يستلزم عدم العلم بالنسخ لا عدم تأخره في الواقع ولا عدم صلوحه ناسخاً، فإذا أجمع به وجب أن لا يكون منسوخاً، وإلا وقع الإجماع على المنسوخ فيكون خطأ، فوجب تأخره ونسخه، والإجماع إنما هو التأخر والنسخ لا أنه ناسخ فافهم . (و) فيه ثالثاً (أن النسخ لا يوجب الخطأ) في الإجماع (كما في النصين (المتواترين) يكون أحدهما ناسخاً للآخر من غير خطأ في أحدهما، فحينئذ لا نسلم أن المنسوخ إن كان قاطعاً فالإجماع خطأ، بل هو قاطع رافع للقاطع الأول (و) فيه رابعاً أنه يستلزم عدم جواز نسخ الآحاد بالمتواتر) لأن الآحاد يتقاعد عن المتواتر فلا تعارض، فلا نسخ كما قلتم في الشق الأخير من الترديد الثاني (أقول : لو أسقط الشق الأول من البين و(قيل) لو كان الإجماع ناسخاً فحينئذ (الأول) المنسوخ إما قطعي أو ظني) إلى الآخر (لكفى) في المطلوب (وحينئذ اندفع الإيرادان (الأولان) لأنهما كانا على قوله إن كان عن نص فهو الناسخ دون الإجماع وقد ارتفع من البين ثم المتناسخان هما الدليلان (المتعارضان لو اتحد زمانهما أي زمان المتعارضين والقطعي والظني لا يتعارضان فلا نسخ بينهما) والإجماع إذ هو قطعي لا ينسخ المظنون ونسخ الآحاد بالمتواتر) كما مر (إنما هو بمعنى عدم البقاء) عنده، وفيه أنه لو كان هذا المعنى لما كان لتقييد كون الآحاد متقدماً ،فائدة، بل المتواتر ناسخ بهذا المعنى تقدم أو تأخر بل الحق أن المتناسخين يجب أن يكون المتقدم واجب العمل وموجباً للحكم الشرعي لولا المتأخر والظني المتقدم. وكذلك فإنه الحكم الشرعي ولو ظنا واجب العمل ما لم يجىء المتأخر ولو سلم أنه يجب التعارض بين المتناسخين فمعناه يجب كونهما، بحيث لولا عروض عارض لكانا متعارضين وإذا كان المتقدم خبراً فهو بحيث لو لم يروه الواحد كان هو والقاطع متعارضين فافهم وكذلك الإجماع متلاش) في زمان) وجود (القطعي) إذ لا مساغ لرأي أحد ولا لفتواه عند معارضة المتواتر فلا يعارضه الإجماع (فلا نسخ حينئذ اندفع (الأخيران الثالث بالأخير والرابع بالأول (فافهم) وفيه نظر ظاهر، أما في الجواب عن الرابع، ، فما عرفت، وأما في الجواب عن الثالث فإنا لا نسلم أن الإجماع متلاش في زمان القاطع، ولا نسلم أنه لا مساغ للرأي عند اجتماعه مع آراء أخرى، وإن لم يكن لرأي واحد مساغ كيف والآراء المجتمعة حجة قاطعة كالنص القاطع فافهم، ولو جوز الإجماع من الإلهام من غير مستند لكان هذا المنع في غاية القوة فافهم فالحق في استدلال ما مر من أن الإجماع الناسخ إن كان عن مستند فهو ثابت من الزمان الشريف، فإذن الناسخ هو وإن كان عن إلهام فهذا الإلهام لا يكون مخالفاً لما ثبت في الشريعة الغراء، فإنّ الشريعة المحمدية لم تدع مصلحة إلا أتت بحكمها، ولا تختلف هذه المصلحة ولا الحكم وقد رضي الله تعالى به، والمنع مكابرة لا يلتفت إليه صاحب أدب بالختم المحمدي فافهم
As for the second point, that consensus cannot be an abrogator: (For the Hanafis, because there is no room for opinion in knowing the end of the ruling's term in Allah's knowledge; rather it is known by revelation). Meaning that abrogation is only lifting the ruling after its existence or stating the term of the ruling. On both counts, there is no doubt that abrogation requires knowledge of the ruling's lifespan, and there is no room for opinion in it. So the people of consensus do not know it, thus they cannot abrogate it. Rather it is known only by revelation, so it is the real abrogator. (I say) It is conceded that pure opinion cannot know the ruling's term, but it does not necessarily imply consensus's inability to abrogate. Perhaps the basis (mustanad) makes it known to them, so after knowing the term via the basis, they rule with a different ruling and know it. (Understand) But this is nothing, because this basis is either pure opinion or revelation; the former is not suitable as a means of knowledge, and on the latter, it is the abrogator, not consensus. It may be objected that opinions have no role in knowing the term of a ruling; it is said: the terms of revealed rulings are unknown, not the terms of rulings derived from consensus. The answer: pure opinion has no role in knowing rulings; rather a legal basis is necessary, and analogy from it does not provide knowledge of the term, and the text is the abrogator – so ponder. Then it is directed to him: it is possible that consensus is without a basis but rather by divine inspiration to the people of consensus, so they may be inspired the term. And you have known what suffices to repel this. (And for others) i.e., for non-Hanafis in this matter: if the abrogating consensus is based on a text, then it (the text) is the real abrogator, not consensus, and consensus is a revealer of this text. Otherwise, i.e., if the abrogating consensus is not based on a text but on analogy or inspiration if allowed: if the first abrogated ruling was a definitive text or definitive consensus, then the abrogating consensus is an error, because opposing the definitive is error. And if the first abrogated ruling was speculative, then with the consensus it does not remain because the condition for acting on it (preponderance via definitiveness which is consensus) is removed. When it does not remain, consensus does not oppose it and thus does not abrogate it. (And there is) first objection: that the abrogation is by the text not consensus, as you said in that first branch, nullifies its authority because then the text is the proof, not consensus, so the premise is invalid. The answer is apparent: because the claimant is not establishing the ruling; rather it (consensus) is a proof in the sense of being a revealer. The establisher is the supporting text, but we do not need to know the basis in order to know the ruling that is agreed upon – it is a revealer of the first/original text, because it is definitive in stating the ruling – so reflect. (And) second objection: that perhaps the supporting text is not known to be later, so it is not suitable as an abrogator, unlike consensus which is known to be later. So we do not accept that if it is based on a text, then the text is the abrogator. The answer is apparent: lack of knowledge of being later only entails lack of knowledge of abrogation, not that it is not later in reality nor that it is not suitable as an abrogator. So if consensus is formed on it, it must not be abrogated; otherwise consensus would have been on an abrogated ruling, which would be an error. So its being later and abrogating is necessitated, and consensus is only the means of knowing the later occurrence and abrogation, not the abrogator itself – understand. (And) third objection: that abrogation does not necessitate error in consensus (as in two mutawatir texts, one abrogates the other without error in either). So we do not accept that if the abrogated is definitive then consensus is error; rather it is a definitive proof raising the first definitive. (And) fourth objection: that it would necessitate the impermissibility of abrogating ahad reports by mutawatir, because ahad fall short of mutawatir, so there is no opposition, hence no abrogation, as you said in the last branch of the second disjunction. (I say) If the first branch is dropped and (it is said) if consensus were an abrogator, then the first abrogated is either definitive or speculative – it suffices for the purpose. And thus the first two objections are repelled because they were based on his statement 'if it is from a text then the text is the abrogator, not consensus', and that has been removed. Then the two abrogating and abrogated evidences are the two contradictory proofs if their times are the same; but definitive and speculative do not contradict, so no abrogation between them. And consensus since it is definitive does not abrogate the speculative. And abrogation of ahad by mutawatir, as mentioned, is only in the sense of non-continuation according to him. There is in it that if this meaning were intended, there would be no benefit in qualifying the ahad as preceding; rather the mutawatir is an abrogator in this sense whether it precedes or follows. But the truth is that in abrogation, the preceding must be obligatorily acted upon and cause a legal ruling were it not for the later, even if the preceding is speculative. Similarly, it is a legal ruling, even if speculative, that must be acted upon until the later comes. And if it is conceded that contradiction must exist between the two abrogating and abrogated, that means they must be such that were it not for an intervening factor, they would contradict. And if the preceding is a khabar, it is such that if the single narrator had not narrated it, it and the definitive would contradict – understand. Similarly, consensus is effaced in the time of the existence of the definitive, because there is no room for anyone's opinion or fatwa when opposing the mutawatir, so consensus does not oppose it. Thus there is no abrogation. Then the last two (third and fourth objections) are repelled: the third by the last point, and the fourth by the first – understand. But there is apparent consideration: as for the answer to the fourth, you have understood; as for the answer to the third, we do not accept that consensus is effaced in the time of the definitive, nor do we accept that there is no room for opinion when it is combined with other opinions. For though there may be no room for a single opinion, how can there be no room when combined opinions are a definitive proof like the definitive text? – understand. And if consensus is allowed from inspiration without basis, then this denial is extremely strong – understand. So the truth in the inference is what has passed: that if the abrogating consensus is based on a basis, it is established from the noble time, so the abrogator is it (the basis). And if it is from inspiration, this inspiration does not oppose what is established in the radiant Sharia, for the Muhammadan Sharia left no benefit except it brought its ruling. This benefit and ruling do not differ, and Allah is pleased with it. And denial is stubbornness that is not heeded by one of good manners in the Muhammadan seal – understand.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This lengthy passage presents the Hanafi argument that consensus (ijma) cannot be an abrogating agent (nasikh). The core reasoning: abrogation requires knowledge of the ruling's duration, which is only known through revelation (wahi), not through human opinion (ra'y). Since ijma is based on opinion, it cannot abrogate. The text then addresses objections from opponents (likely non-Hanafis). Objections include: (1) if ijma is based on a text, the text is the real abrogator, so ijma has no authority; (2) the text's timing may be unknown, while ijma's timing is clear; (3) abrogation does not imply error in ijma, as two mutawatir texts can abrogate; (4) if ijma is definitive, it cannot abrogate speculative rulings, and ahad reports cannot be abrogated by mutawatir. The Hanafi reply elaborates: ijma serves as a revealer (kashif) of the text, not the abrogator; the timing issue is resolved by assuming the text is later; abrogation can occur without error; and the fourth objection is refuted by distinguishing between ahad and mutawatir. The author then synthesizes: if ijma is based on a basis (mustanad), that basis is the abrogator; if based on inspiration, it cannot contradict Sharia. The overall conclusion is that ijma does not abrogate.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation – the lifting of a legal ruling by a later evidence from the Lawgiver.
إجماع (ijma): The consensus of mujtahidun on a legal ruling.
مستند (mustanad): The basis or evidence upon which a ruling is founded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why cannot consensus (ijma) abrogate a ruling?
A) Because consensus is not a source of Islamic law.
B) Because abrogation requires knowledge of the ruling's duration, which only revelation provides.
C) Because consensus can only confirm rulings, not change them.
D) Because later consensus cannot form after disagreement.

Key Takeaway
Consensus cannot abrogate because abrogation is a revelatory act requiring knowledge of the ruling's lifespan, which human opinion cannot provide.

Naskh — Abrogation

Ijma Cannot Abrogate the Qur'an: The Case of the Mother's Share
Refuting the claim that Companions' consensus abrogated the Qur'anic ruling on mother's share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the claim that ijma can abrogate the Qur'an and apply the Hanafi position using three counter-arguments.

Core Idea
Ijma cannot abrogate the Qur'an; it only clarifies or points to the true abrogator.

This passage addresses a critical usul al-fiqh dispute: whether the consensus of the Companions can abrogate a Qur'anic ruling. The example is the mother's inheritance share with two brothers. The Hanafi school refutes this claim with three distinct arguments, each grounded in the nature of naskh and the role of ijma. Understanding these arguments strengthens your ability to distinguish true abrogation from interpretation and specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opposing Claim
Some argued that Uthman's ruling reducing the mother's share with two brothers constituted naskh of the Qur'anic verse by ijma. Pinpoint this claim in the text.
The claim is introduced by the phrase 'فقد نسخ القوم الكتاب بإجماعهم'.
2
Extract the First Hanafi Argument
The verse was silent (sakita) about the specific case of two brothers. Uthman's ruling was interpretation (tafsir) based on ijma, not abrogation. Locate this in the text.
Look for 'الآية ساكتة عن حال الأم مع الأخوين'.
3
Extract the Second Hanafi Argument
The term 'ikhwa' (brothers) was used metaphorically (majaz) for more than one, and metaphorical usage is not naskh. Find this argument.
It appears after 'معناه أي معنى قول أمير المؤمنين الإخوة مجاز'.
4
Extract the Third Hanafi Argument
Even if the Companions performed naskh, that would be based on an actual abrogator (nasikh), and ijma would only be evidence (dalil) for that abrogator, not the abrogation itself. Locate the conditional 'لو سلم'.
This argument parallels the rule that a Companion's action contrary to a text points to an abrogator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنتم تردون الأم من الثلث إلى السدس بأخوين مع أنهما ليسا إخوة (أجاب) أمير المؤمنين وإمام الأحيين (عثمان) رضي الله تعالى عنه (حجبها قومك يا غلام يعني من الثلث إلى السدس بأخوين، وقد مر تخريجه فقد نسخ القوم الكتاب بإجماعهم (قلنا) أولاً: إن الآية ساكتة عن حال الأم مع الأخوين وكان أمير المؤمنين ردها في هذا الحال من الثلث إلى السدس، فسأل ابن عباس أن الآية لا تتناولها فاستدل أمير المؤمنين بالإجماع فيما سكت عنه الكتاب، وهذا ليس من النسخ في شيء وهو ظاهر جداً، وقلنا ثانياً : (معناه) أي معنى قول أمير المؤمنين الإخوة (مجاز) عما فوق الواحد (بالإجماع، وهو) أي التجوز ليس نسخاً بالإجماع فليس من الباب أصلاً (و) قلنا ثالثاً : (لو سلم أن القوم نسخوا بما لاح لهم من الدليل وهو الناسخ حقيقة (فهو) أي الإجماع (دليل) على الناسخ، كعمل الصحابي خلاف الناص المفسر فإنه دليل على الناسخ) فافهم .
And you reject the mother from a third to a sixth with two brothers even though they are not brothers. (Answer) The Commander of the Faithful and Imam of the two eras, Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) said: "Your people prevented her, O boy, meaning from a third to a sixth with two brothers, and its derivation has already passed, for the people abrogated the Book by their consensus." (We say) Firstly: The verse is silent about the case of the mother with two brothers, and the Commander of the Faithful reduced her in this case from a third to a sixth. Ibn Abbas asked that the verse does not address it, so the Commander of the Faithful argued by consensus in what the Book was silent about, and this is not abrogation at all, and it is very clear. And we say secondly: (Meaning) i.e., the meaning of the Commander of the Faithful's statement "brothers" is metaphorical for more than one (by consensus), and it (i.e., the metaphorical usage) is not abrogation by consensus, so it is not from the subject at all. And (we say) thirdly: (If it were granted that the people abrogated by what appeared to them of evidence, and it is the true abrogator, then it (i.e., consensus) is evidence for the abrogator, like the action of a Companion contrary to an explicit text is evidence for the abrogator.) So understand.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that the Companions abrogated a Qur'anic verse by their consensus. The author presents three arguments: first, the verse was silent about the specific case of the mother with two brothers, so Uthman's ruling was an interpretation based on ijma, not an abrogation. Second, the term 'ikhwa' (brothers) is used metaphorically for more than one, and metaphorical usage is not naskh. Third, even if the Companions performed naskh, their ijma was evidence for an actual abrogator, not the abrogation itself. The author emphasizes that ijma cannot abrogate the Qur'an; it can only clarify or point to an abrogating proof.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma): The consensus of the mujtahidun of the ummah after the death of the Prophet.
نسخ (naskh): The abrogation of a ruling by a later revealed text.
مجاز (majaz): Figurative use of language; here, 'ikhwa' used figuratively for more than one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the claim that the Companions abrogated the Qur'anic ruling on the mother's share?
A) By saying the verse was silent about two brothers.
B) By saying the term 'ikhwa' is metaphorical.
C) By saying ijma is evidence for the abrogator.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Ijma cannot abrogate the Qur'an; it can only clarify or point to an abrogating proof.

Naskh — Abrogation

Distinguishing Naskh from Intiha al-Hukm bi Intiha al-'Illa
Explaining the Companions' consensus to drop mu'allafa share is not naskh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between naskh (abrogation) and intiha al-hukm bi intiha al-'illa (expiry of ruling due to expiry of cause) and apply this distinction to the Companions' dropping of the mu'allafa share.

Core Idea
The dropping of the mu'allafa share was not abrogation; it was the natural expiry of a ruling when its cause ceased.

In this lesson, we examine a key usul dispute: when the Companions stopped giving zakat to mu'allafatu qulubuhum, was this an abrogation (naskh) by ijma? The Hanafi response clarifies that it was not naskh but rather the expiry of the ruling due to the expiry of its cause, a principle known as intiha al-hukm bi intiha al-'illa. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper usul reasoning, as conflating the two can lead to erroneous claims about the completeness of the Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical event
The Companions under Abu Bakr stopped giving zakat to mu'allafatu qulubuhum. This is reported as an apparent consensus.
2
Recognize the conflicting claim
Some argue that this is an instance of naskh (abrogation) by ijma, i.e., the ruling in the Quran was abrogated by the consensus of the Companions.
The opposing side uses the consensus as evidence of abrogation.
3
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position is that this is not naskh but rather intiha al-hukm bi intiha al-'illa: the ruling expires because its cause (the need to strengthen Islam by winning over influential figures) ceased to exist.
The term 'mu'allafatu qulubuhum' itself indicates the cause.
4
Analyze the evidence
The Hanafi evidence includes prophetic indications and the linguistic indication of the term 'mu'allafatu qulubuhum', which shows that the ruling was conditioned on the presence of the cause.
No new revelation or abrogating verse is involved.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
If the cause returns (e.g., Islam becomes weak again), the ruling could be revived. This practical consequence shows that it is not a permanent abrogation.
This distinguishes the case from true naskh where the ruling is permanently replaced.

وقالوا ثانياً : سقط سهم المؤلفة من الزكاة بإجماع الصحابة في زمن خليفة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله تعالى وعنهم، روى الطبراني عن أمير المؤمنين وإمام الأعدلين عمر رضي الله عنه لما أتاه عيينة ابن حصن قال : الْحَقُّ مِن رَّبِّكُمْ فَمَن شَاءَ فَلْيُؤْمِن وَمَن شَاءَ فَلْيَكْفُرْ ﴾ [الكهف: ٢٩] يعني اليوم ليس مؤلفة ولم ينكره أحد من الصحابة فصار إجماعاً كذا في التيسير» (قلنا) هذا (من قبيل انتهاء الحكم لانتهاء العلة) المعلومة للصحابة بالإشارات النبوية، وفي التعبير عنهم بالمؤلفة القلوب إشارة أيضاً إلى ذلك، فإنهم إنما كانوا يعطون لإعزاز الدين بهم ، والآن صار عزيزاً من غير معونتهم حتى قيل : الإعزاز الآن في عدم الدفع إليهم) وهو ظاهر (وهذا) أي انتهاء الحكم لانتهاء العلة (لا يسمى نسخاً، لأنه انتهاء جلي) معلوم قبل وجود ما يتوهم ناسخاً، بل الحكم موقت به فسقط ما أن كل نسخ كذلك، فإنه انتهاء للحكم لانتهاء العلة لاستحالة ارتفاع بقاء العلة، وقد يتوهم أيضاً أنه كما أنهم علموا انتهاء الحكم في هذه الصورة يمكن عنه يتوهم الحكم مع أن يعلموا في صورة أخرى بعد زمان انتفاء العلة، فيحكمون بانتهاء الحكم وهو النسخ بالإجماع، ولا تصغ إليه فإنا قد بينا أن الله تعالى أكمل الشريعة المحمدية حتى لن يبق حكم يطلع عليه بعده عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام فلا يعلم انتهاء حكم إلا بإعلامه بالوحي صلوات الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلامه ولا يجترىء على منعه مسلم، وقد بينه الشيخ الأكبر قدس سره في مواضع عديدة من كتبه الكرام.
And they secondly said: The share of those whose hearts are to be reconciled (mu'allafatu qulubuhum) fell from zakat by the consensus of the Companions in the time of the Caliph of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and Companions), Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him and them). Al-Tabarani narrated from the Commander of the Faithful and Imam of the most just, Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that when 'Uyaynah ibn Hisn came to him, he said: "The truth is from your Lord; so whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve" [Quran 18:29], meaning today there is no mu'allaf, and no one among the Companions denied it, so it became a consensus, as in al-Taysir. (We say) This is of the type of the expiry of a ruling due to the expiry of its cause, which was known to the Companions through prophetic indications. And in their being called 'mu'allafatu qulubuhum' there is also an indication of that, for they were only given to strengthen the religion through them, and now it has become strong without their assistance, so much so that it was said: strengthening now lies in not giving to them. And this is apparent. And this (i.e., the expiry of the ruling due to the expiry of the cause) is not called abrogation, because it is a clear expiry known before the existence of what is imagined to be an abrogator. Rather, the ruling is temporally conditioned by it, so it falls. Not every abrogation is like that, for it is the expiry of a ruling due to the expiry of the cause, because it is impossible for the cause to remain while the ruling is lifted. And it might also be imagined that just as they knew the expiry of the ruling in this case, they might know in another case after some time the disappearance of the cause, and they would judge the expiry of the ruling, which is abrogation by consensus. Do not listen to that, for we have explained that Allah has perfected the Muhammadan Shari'ah so that no ruling remains to be discovered after him (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and Companions). Therefore, the expiry of a ruling is not known except by revelation from Allah (blessings and peace be upon him and his family and Companions), and no Muslim dares to deny it. The Greatest Shaykh (may his secret be sanctified) has explained this in many places in his noble books.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage addresses the claim that the Companions abrogated the share for mu'allafatu qulubuhum by ijma. The author explains that this is not naskh but rather the natural expiry of the ruling because its cause (i'zaz al-din) had ceased. The Companions understood from prophetic indications that the ruling was temporally conditioned. When the cause disappeared, the ruling automatically ended. This is called 'intiha al-hukm bi intiha al-'illa' and is distinct from naskh, which involves a new divine command. The author warns against the misconception that such changes constitute abrogation, affirming that Allah completed the Shari'ah and no further abrogation occurs after the Prophet's death.

Key Terms
مؤلفة قلوبهم (mu'allafatu qulubuhum): Those whose hearts are to be reconciled, a category of zakat recipients.
انتهاء الحكم بانتهاء العلة (intiha al-hukm bi intiha al-'illa): The expiry of a ruling upon the expiry of its cause.
علة ('illa): The effective cause or ratio legis of a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why was the share of mu'allafatu qulubuhum dropped by the Companions?
A) Because the verse was abrogated by ijma.
B) Because the cause (i'zaz al-din) ceased to exist.
C) Because the Companions forgot the ruling.
D) Because of a new revelation.

Key Takeaway
The dropping of the mu'allafa share is not an instance of naskh but of the expiry of a ruling due to the expiry of its cause, a key distinction in Hanafi usul.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
15 min
Does Qiyas Allow Naskh? The Hanafi Position
Debate on whether analogical reasoning can undergo or effect abrogation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position that ordinary qiyas cannot function as nasikh or mansukh, and distinguish the exception for qiyas with mansus illah.

Core Idea
Ordinary qiyas is too weak for naskh; only qiyas with an explicit illah acts like a nass.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut plunges into one of the most subtle debates in usul al-fiqh: can analogical reasoning be abrogated or abrogate other proofs? The Hanafi school holds a strict position: qiyas, by itself, cannot enter into naskh. But there is a narrow exception when the illah (cause) is explicitly stated in the text. In this lesson, we will unpack the arguments, the key distinction between extracted and explicit illah, and why the Companions' practice is the ultimate evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim and its basis
The author opens by arguing that qiyas cannot be abrogated because its condition (being preponderant) disappears when a contradictory proof appears, so it collapses and cannot be abrogated. The condition for naskh – a genuine contradiction between two contemporaneous proofs – is missing.
This is the initial logical argument.
2
Analyze the counterarguments and the response regarding extracted qiyas
Some object that qiyas could be lifted by a stronger proof. The author reports the view from Matali' al-Asrar that qiyas with extracted illah is so weak it never truly contradicts a nass. The author critiques this by noting that if qiyas can specify (takhsis), it could theoretically also abrogate, but the school rejects this for naskh.
The distinction between extracted and explicit illah is introduced.
3
Examine the exception: qiyas with mansus illah is like nass
Ibn al-Hajib's view that qiyas with definitive illah can abrogate during the Prophet's lifetime is discussed. The author ultimately takes the position that only when the illah is explicit (mansus) and its presence in the branch is certain, and no preventers exist, does qiyas become like a nass and can enter naskh.
This is the final Hanafi position.
4
Evaluate the Companions' practice as evidence
The strongest Hanafi proof is the practice of the Sahaba: they never used qiyas to oppose an existing ruling from a nass. The passage cites that it is not reported that they sought qiyas to lift an established ruling. This indicates that qiyas was not considered a valid abrogator.
This is a key dalil for the Hanafi school.
5
Understand the debate on takhsis al-azman and why the Hanafi school rejects it for naskh
Opponents argue that naskh is like specification of time, and qiyas can specify times as it specifies individuals. The Hanafi response: determining the end of a ruling's duration is beyond opinion-based ijtihad; it requires revelation. If a ruling's cause disappears, that is not naskh but removal of the cause.
This distinguishes naskh from mere cessation of cause.

الأصل الأول الكتاب وهو ناسخاً له فلا أنه · 1.1 أن القياس لا يكون منسوخاً فلأن شرط العمل به رجحانه وقد زال بوجود المعارض) وهو الذي يتوهم ناسخاً، وإذا انتفى شرط العمل فلا حجية فيه فلا رفع به) وهذا لو تم وهو في حيّز الخفاء، فإن العام المخصوص يجوز تخصيصه به عندنا وتخصيص العام مطلقاً عند الشافعية ومن الفطريات أن المرجوح لا يغيّر الراجح، وإذ قد صلح مغير النص فليصلح رافعاً لما ثبت به ويكون مرتفعاً مثله في على أصل ثم علم قياس آخر على أصل آخر متأخر عنه، ويكون هذا القياس معارضاً إياه يحكم بانتساخ الأول من الثاني لوجود دليلين مفيدين للحكمين، فيرفع المتأخر المقدم وليس هذا مجالاً للرأي المحض في نصب الأحكام، بل إنما هو نصب من الشارع دليلاً من عنده موجباً لانتهاء عمر الحكم، فإن العلة بنص قط قلت : لعل مقصوده أن القياس المستخرج الآن قياس معتبر من الزمان الشريف فناسخيته ومنسوخيته من ذلك الزمان، وإنما ظهر للمجتهد الآن وليس يمكن انتساخ حكم ثابت من الشرع بقياس اعتبره الشارع الآن فإنه لو كان لزم المجال للرأي في معرفة مدة الحكم، قلت : صحيح، كيف لا ولو كان القياس معتبراً الآن ومفيد الحكم جديد لزم نصب الشرع. وإثبات حكم جديد خلا عنه شريعة الخاتم المطهرة المكملة لكن على هذا يكون هذا الفرق قليل الجدوى، فإن كل نسخ سواء كان للقياس أو للنص وبالقياس وبالنص، كذلك لا يجوز إلا في الزمان الشريف فافهم. والحق أن هذا كله جدل والقياس لا يصلح ناسخاً ولا منسوخاً أصلاً إلا إذا اتفق أن تكون العلة منصوصة، ويكون وجودها في الفرع مقطوعاً، وكذا عدم كونه وعدم كون الأصل شرطاً، فإنه حينئذ يكون كالنص، وذلك لأن الصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم إنما يستعملون الرأي عند عدم وجدان نص ثابت الحكم ولو في حين ما علم منه أنهم لا يجعلون الرأي معارضاً لحكم معمول للنص وإن كان ظنياً كيف ولم ينقل عنهم طلب القياس ليكون رافعاً لحكم معمول كما تدل عليه الوقائع الكثيرة وإنكار هذا بعيد عن الإنصاف، وهذا بخلاف القياس المخصص فإنهم كانوا يؤولون النصوص الظنية بالرأي، ويجعلون الرأي قرينة على تغير ظاهر النص، ويؤيده ما قال الشيخ الأكبر خاتم الولاية المحمدية قدس سره الشريف أن القياس ليس حجة مطلقة بل إنما اعتبر عند عدم وجود نص وإجماع الضرورة العمل لئلا تخلو الواقعة عما يعمل به المكلف هذا مفقود في القياس والنص. وأما القياسان المتعارضان فالظاهر أن متقدم الأصل منسوخ بمتأخره، كيف لا والأصل المتقدم كان دالاً على حكم الفرع بواسطة العلة، وكذا الأصل المتأخر دل على ضد ذلك الحكم فيه بوساطة علته، غاية ما في الباب أن دلالتهما ظنية والقياس إنما هو بالحقيقة يرجع إلى انتساخ النص المظنون بالنص الآخر مثله في بعض مدلوله، لكن هذا الانتساخ كان من قبل في زمانه الشريف، ولا يجوز العمل بقياس منسوخ بحال لكونه منسوخاً من زمن الشارع وبقاء معارضه في نظر الشارع، وإنما علم هذا الانتساخ الآن. وهذا بعينه، كما إذا انتسخ نص بنص فقد ارتفع حكم المنسوخ من الأصل وإن خفي على المجتهد برهة من الزمان، ثم ظهر هذا كله ظاهراً إلا أنه لم ينقل عن الصحابة في مناظراتهم ترجيح القياس بتقدم أصل أحدهما على الآخر فتدبر تدبراً صادقاً والله أعلم بأسرار أحكامه. مجيز وناسخية القياس (قالوا) النسخ تخصيص الأزمان فإنه إبانة عمر الحكم والتخصيص في الأزمان كالتخصيص في الأعيان وتخصيص الأعيان به جائز فكذا تخصيص الأزمان (قلنا مماثلة تخصيص الأزمان والأعيان (ممنوعة إذ لا مجال للرأي في درك الانتهاء لمدة الحكم فإن قلت: يجوز أن تكون المصلحة في حكم موجودة إلى زمان من الأزمان، فينتهي الحكم إليه ويدرك فيه بالرأي قال ولو علم الحكم منوطاً بمصلحة ثم علم ارتفاعها فكسهم المؤلفة أي فهو انتفاء الحكم لانتفاء العلة كما في سهم المؤلفة، وهذا ليس من النسخ في شيء، فإنه رفع من الشارع الحكم الثابت، هذا ولك أن تقول : إن تخصيص الأزمان بالقياس ليس بالرأي المحض حتى يكون كاشف عن هذه الدلالة فهذا
The first principle is the Book. And it is not abrogating it? ... That qiyas cannot be abrogated because the condition for acting upon it is its strength, and that has ceased due to the existence of the objection (which is thought to be abrogating). And if the condition for acting is absent, then it has no authority, so no abrogation (can be effected by it). And even if this were valid, it would indicate the first point also: that for abrogation, it is necessary that the two proofs be such that if they were assumed contemporaneous, they would be contradictory. Qiyas collapses when opposed by a proof (nass), so it cannot be abrogated by a proof. It is not objected that every abrogation requires contradiction and the condition for acting is its absence, so no abrogation is possible at all. Similarly, it cannot be objected that it is permissible for qiyas to be lifted by a contradictory proof or to lift it, so the condition for acting is not negated due to the persistence of contradiction. Then there remains here that we do not concede the collapse of qiyas when opposed by a proof; rather, qiyas is a legitimate proof like another proof. So if it does not collapse and takes precedence over the other proof, it is lifted by it; if it is later, it lifts it. It is also possible for a qiyas with an earlier original to be abrogated by a later qiyas, and qiyas does not collapse when facing another qiyas. Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiya said (my father, may Allah sanctify his soul, thought the more likely view is that qiyas with extracted illah (weak analogy) has a weak presumption about its illah because it is based on opinion, and then the ruling established in the branch by its existence is even weaker. So it does not remain when faced with a text indicating otherwise, thus no contradiction is realized if we assume contemporaneity, so no abrogating or abrogated status. As for its being not abrogated by a similar qiyas and its not abrogating it, it is because analogies do not contradict each other as established in the section on contradiction; rather, preference (tarjih) is required; if not agreed, the mujtahid may act on whichever he wishes. Abrogation is a branch of contradiction. As for the explicit illah (mansus al-illah), it is like the concept of approval (mafhum al-muwafaqa). End of his noble words. And this is based on the idea that extracted qiyas is inferior to nass and is not considered when opposed. This is somewhat obscure, for the particularized general (al-amm al-makhsus) can be specified by it according to us, and by the general absolutely according to the Shafi'is. It is axiomatic that the inferior does not change the superior. But if it can change the nass, then it can lift what is established by it, and it is elevated similar in indication, and there is no harm in it at all. As for qiyas when facing another similar qiyas, they are also contradictory because each produces the opposite of what the other produces, which is contradiction. They are not discarded because there is no proof inferior to them to turn to; rather, preference is sought; if not found, the heart decides, lest action proceed without evidence. If one has a later original, it has preponderance and lifts the earlier illah. As for the explicit illah (mansus al-illah), Ibn al-Hajib said it is permissible to abrogate the definitive qiyas by another definitive qiyas during his (the Prophet's) life, and after him, it is not permissible because there is no room for opinion. It was objected that qiyas cannot be definitive even if the illah is definitive because the branch might have a preventer or the original might have a condition. If we assume it definitive, it would be like a nass, abrogating and being abrogated. Perhaps he meant definitive in illah, so the objection does not arise. Yes, it is objected that the distinction is arbitrary, for qiyas in his noble time and after it are equal in authority and in conveying rulings. So if one now knows a qiyas on an original, then knows another qiyas on another later original, and this qiyas opposes the first, one judges the first abrogated by the second due to the existence of two proofs conveying two rulings. The later lifts the earlier. This is not a matter of pure opinion in establishing rulings; rather, it is the Lawgiver establishing a proof from Himself causing the end of the ruling's duration. For the illah by nass is decisive. I said: Perhaps he meant that the qiyas derived now is a valid qiyas from the noble era, so its abrogating or being abrogated is from that era; it only appears to the mujtahid now, and it is not possible for a ruling established from the Shari'ah to be abrogated by a qiyas now considered by the Lawgiver, for if so, it would open the door for opinion in knowing the duration of the ruling. I said: Correct. How could it not be? For if qiyas were considered now and produced a new ruling, it would necessitate establishing a new ruling missing from the perfected and complete Shari'ah of the Seal. But on this view, the distinction is of little benefit, for every abrogation, whether of qiyas or by qiyas, is like (abrogation) of nass and by nass; it is not permissible except in the noble era. So understand. The truth is that all this is debate, and qiyas is not valid as an abrogator nor as abrogated at all except if the illah is explicit, its existence in the branch is definitive, and the absence of any preventer and that the original is not conditional. Then it is like a nass. This is because the Companions used opinion only when no nass with established ruling was found; they never made opinion oppose an existing ruling of a nass even if zanni. How could it be? It is not reported that they sought a qiyas to lift an existing ruling, as shown by many incidents. Denial of this is far from fairness. This is unlike the qiyas that particularizes (al-qiyas al-mukhassis), for they used to interpret zanni nusus with opinion and made opinion a qarina for changing the apparent meaning of the nass. This is supported by what the greatest Shaykh, the Seal of Muhammadi Wilaya (may Allah sanctify his noble soul) said: 'Qiyas is not an absolute proof; it is only considered when there is no nass and no consensus out of necessity for action so that no event is without something for the mukallaf to act upon.' This (necessity) is absent in the case of qiyas and nass together. As for two contradictory analogies, the apparent view is that the earlier original is abrogated by the later one. Why not? The earlier original indicated a ruling for the branch via the illah, and the later original indicated the opposite ruling via its illah. At most, their indications are zanni, and qiyas in reality returns to the abrogation of a zanni nass by another similar nass in part of its meaning. But this abrogation was in the noble era, and it is not permissible to act upon an abrogated qiyas at all because it was abrogated from the Lawgiver's time and its opponent remains in the Lawgiver's view. This abrogation is only known now. This is exactly like when a nass is abrogated by another nass; the ruling of the abrogated is lifted from the root even if hidden from the mujtahid for a while, then appears. All this is apparent, except that it is not reported from the Companions in their debates that they preferred qiyas by the precedence of one original over another. So reflect truly and Allah knows best the secrets of His rulings. (They said) Abrogation is the specification of times (takhsis al-azman) because it is the delimitation of the ruling's duration. Specification (takhsis) in times is like specification in individuals. Specification of individuals by qiyas is permissible, so likewise specification of times. We said: The analogy between specification of times and individuals is denied, because there is no room for opinion in perceiving the end of a ruling's duration. If you say: It is possible that the maslaha in a ruling exists until a certain time, so the ruling ends at that time, and this can be perceived by opinion. He said: If a ruling is known to be dependent on a maslaha, and then its rise is known, like the share of the muallafat al-qulub (those whose hearts are reconciled), then it is the negation of the ruling due to the negation of the cause, as in the share of the muallafa. This is not abrogation at all, because it is the Lawgiver's lifting of an established ruling. This, but you may say: The specification of times by qiyas is not pure opinion so as to be a discoverer of this indication. So this.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is an extensive usul al-fiqh dispute concerning whether qiyas can be subject to or perform naskh. The author presents and critiques multiple positions. The opening argues that qiyas cannot be abrogated because its condition for validity (being preponderant) is lost when a contradictory proof appears; hence it collapses. Against the objection that abrogation would then be impossible, the author clarifies that naskh requires proof of contradiction, which is absent here. The discussion then presents a contrary view: qiyas might be lifted by a stronger proof. The author reports from Matali' al-Asrar the view that qiyas (with extracted illah) is too weak to enter into contradiction, so naskh is irrelevant. The author critiques this, noting that if qiyas can specify a general text (takhsis), it can also act as an abrogator. The passage then discusses Ibn al-Hajib's view that qiyas with definitive illah can abrogate during the Prophet's life only. The author finds the distinction arbitrary and argues that qiyas in the Prophet's era and later are equal in authority. Eventually, the author's final position is that qiyas is not valid for naskh at all, except if the illah is explicit (mansus) and its application is definitive—then it is like a nass. This is supported by the practice of the Companions who never opposed a nass with qiyas. The passage ends with a debate (qaalu-qulna) where opponents argue that naskh is like takhsis al-azman, and qiyas can specify times. The author responds that determining the end of a ruling is beyond opinion-based ijtihad; if a ruling is seen to have ended due to change in its cause, that is not naskh but removal of the cause. The final line allows the possibility that takhsis al-azman by qiyas is not pure opinion but a discovery of an indication.

Key Terms
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation: the lifting of a previously established Shari'ah ruling by a later evidence, indicating its duration has ended.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared illah.
العلة المنصوصة (al-illah al-mansusa): An explicit cause (illah) stated in the text (Qur'an or Sunnah) for a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, can qiyas be abrogated (mansukh) by another qiyas?
A) Yes, if the later qiyas is based on a later original.
B) No, because qiyas cannot be abrogated at all.
C) Only if the illah is mansus and its existence in the branch is definitive.
D) Only if the Companions did so.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas, the analogical reasoning, is too weak to enter into the system of naskh; only when its cause is explicitly stated by the Lawgiver does it acquire the strength of a direct text.

Naskh — Abrogation

Qiyas as Nasikh and Mansukh: The Hanafi Position
Debate on whether qiyas can abrogate or be abrogated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether qiyas can abrogate or be abrogated, and evaluate the opposing argument using Hanafi usul principles.

Core Idea
Qiyas is neither a valid abrogator nor abrogated; only when the 'illa is textual and certain does it resemble a text, but it never overturns established rulings.

This passage, from Fawatih al-Rahamut, addresses a subtle usul dispute: can qiyas (analogical reasoning) serve as an abrogator (nasikh) or be subject to abrogation (mansukh)? The Hanafi position is a firm 'no'—qiyas is a subordinate proof that operates only in the absence of text or consensus. The passage lays out the arguments and responds to those who would permit abrogation through qiyas. Understanding this distinction safeguards the hierarchy of proofs in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on qiyas as nasikh/mansukh
The author asserts that qiyas is not suitable as an abrogator or abrogated, except when the 'illa is textual and certain in the branch, making it like a text itself.
2
Identify the opposing argument
The opponent argues that naskh is specification of duration, analogous to specification of individuals by qiyas, which is permissible; thus qiyas can specify durations and hence abrogate.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The analogy is rejected because opinion (ra'y) has no role in determining the end of a ruling's duration. If a ruling depends on maslaha, its cessation lifts the ruling by removal of 'illa, not by naskh.
4
Examine the exception
The Hanafi position allows that if the 'illa is textual and its existence in the branch is certain, the qiyas has the strength of a text (nass) and may be treated accordingly, but this is not abrogation by qiyas per se.
5
Derive the practical implication
In practice, a mujtahid cannot use qiyas to overturn a ruling established by a clear text; the text prevails, ensuring stability of Shariah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لزم المجال للرأي في معرفة مدة الحكم، قلت : صحيح، ، كيف لا ولو كان القياس معتبراً الآن ومفيد الحكم جديد لزم نصب الشرع. وإثبات حكم جديد خلا عنه شريعة الخاتم المطهرة المكملة لكن على هذا يكون هذا الفرق قليل الجدوى، فإن كل نسخ سواء كان للقياس أو للنص وبالقياس وبالنص، كذلك لا يجوز إلا في الزمان الشريف فافهم. والحق أن هذا كله جدل والقياس لا يصلح ناسخاً ولا منسوخاً أصلاً إلا إذا اتفق أن تكون العلة منصوصة، ويكون وجودها في الفرع مقطوعاً، وكذا عدم كونه وعدم كون الأصل شرطاً، فإنه حينئذ يكون كالنص، وذلك لأن الصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم إنما يستعملون الرأي عند عدم وجدان نص ثابت الحكم ولو في حين ما المخصص فإنهم كانوا يؤولون النصوص الظنية بالرأي، ويجعلون الرأي قرينة على تغير ظاهر النص، ويؤيده ما قال الشيخ الأكبر خاتم الولاية المحمدية قدس سره الشريف أن القياس ليس حجة مطلقة بل إنما اعتبر عند عدم وجود نص وإجماع الضرورة العمل لئلا تخلو الواقعة عما يعمل به المكلف هذا مفقود في القياس والنص. وأما القياسان المتعارضان فالظاهر أن متقدم الأصل منسوخ بمتأخره، كيف لا والأصل المتقدم كان دالاً على حكم الفرع بواسطة العلة، وكذا الأصل المتأخر دل على ضد ذلك الحكم فيه بوساطة علته، غاية ما في الباب أن دلالتهما ظنية والقياس إنما هو بالحقيقة يرجع إلى انتساخ النص المظنون بالنص الآخر مثله في بعض مدلوله، لكن هذا الانتساخ كان من قبل في زمانه الشريف، ولا يجوز العمل بقياس منسوخ بحال لكونه منسوخاً من زمن الشارع وبقاء معارضه في نظر الشارع، وإنما علم هذا الانتساخ الآن. وهذا بعينه، كما إذا انتسخ نص بنص فقد ارتفع حكم المنسوخ من الأصل وإن خفي على المجتهد برهة من الزمان، ثم ظهر هذا كله ظاهراً إلا أنه لم ينقل عن الصحابة في مناظراتهم ترجيح القياس بتقدم أصل أحدهما على الآخر فتدبر تدبراً صادقاً والله أعلم بأسرار أحكامه. مجيز وناسخية القياس (قالوا) النسخ تخصيص الأزمان فإنه إبانة عمر الحكم والتخصيص في الأزمان كالتخصيص في الأعيان وتخصيص الأعيان به جائز فكذا تخصيص الأزمان (قلنا مماثلة تخصيص الأزمان والأعيان (ممنوعة إذ لا مجال للرأي في درك الانتهاء لمدة الحكم فإن قلت: يجوز أن تكون المصلحة في حكم موجودة إلى زمان من الأزمان، فينتهي الحكم إليه ويدرك فيه بالرأي قال ولو علم الحكم منوطاً بمصلحة ثم علم ارتفاعها فكسهم المؤلفة أي فهو انتفاء الحكم لانتفاء العلة كما في سهم المؤلفة، وهذا ليس من النسخ في شيء، فإنه رفع من الشارع الحكم الثابت، هذا ولك أن تقول : إن تخصيص الأزمان بالقياس ليس بالرأي المحض حتى يكون كاشف عن هذه الدلالة فهذا الأصل الأول/ الكتاب ١٠٣ درك الانتهاء به بل بنصب حجة من الشارع كما مر فهما سواء فلا بد من الرجوع إلى ما قلنا فتذكر .
I said: Perhaps his intention is that the qiyas derived now is a qiyas considered from the noble time, so its abrogating and abrogated status is from that time. It only became apparent to the mujtahid now, and it is not possible to abrogate a ruling established from the Shariah by a qiyas that the Lawgiver considered now, because if that were the case, it would necessitate room for opinion in knowing the duration of the ruling. I said: Correct. Indeed, if qiyas were considered now and beneficial for a new ruling, it would necessitate establishing new legislation and proving a new ruling lacking in the complete and purified Shariah of the Seal. But upon this, this difference is of little benefit, for every abrogation, whether by qiyas or by text, and whether through qiyas or through text, is only permissible in the noble time, so understand. The truth is that all of this is dialectic, and qiyas is not suitable as an abrogator nor as an abrogated at all, except if it happens that the 'illa is textual, and its existence in the branch is certain, and likewise its non-existence and the non-existence of a condition in the origin, for then it is like a text. This is because the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, only use opinion when they do not find a text with established ruling, even if at some time it is known from them that they do not make opinion oppose a ruling acted upon by a text, even if it is speculative. How not, when it is not transmitted from them that they sought qiyas to lift an established ruling, as many incidents indicate, and denying this is far from fairness. This is unlike qiyas for specification, for they would interpret speculative texts by opinion, and make opinion a presumption for changing the apparent meaning of the text. This is supported by what the Greatest Shaykh, the Seal of Muhammadan Sainthood, may his noble secret be sanctified, said: that qiyas is not an absolute proof, but is only considered when there is no text or consensus out of necessity for action, lest an incident be devoid of something by which the responsible person acts. This is absent in qiyas and text. As for two conflicting qiyases, it is apparent that the earlier origin is abrogated by the later one. Why not? The earlier origin indicated the ruling of the branch through the 'illa, and likewise the later origin indicated the opposite of that ruling in it through its 'illa. The utmost in this matter is that their indications are speculative, and qiyas in reality reverts to abrogation of a speculative text by another like it in some of its implication. However, this abrogation occurred previously in the noble time, and it is not permissible to act on an abrogated qiyas in any case because it is abrogated since the time of the Lawgiver, and its opposite remains in the view of the Lawgiver. This abrogation is only known now. This is exactly like when a text is abrogated by a text: the ruling of the abrogated is lifted from the beginning, even if it was hidden from the mujtahid for a period of time, then it becomes apparent. All this is apparent, except that it is not transmitted from the Companions in their debates that they preferred one qiyas over another due to the precedence of one of its origins. So reflect sincerely, and Allah knows best the secrets of His rulings. One who permits abrogation through qiyas (said): Abrogation is specification of durations, for it is clarification of the duration of the ruling. Specification in durations is like specification in individuals, and specification of individuals by it is permissible, so likewise specification of durations. (We said): The analogy between specification of durations and individuals is not admitted, for there is no room for opinion in grasping the end of the ruling's duration. If you say: It is possible that the maslaha in a ruling exists until a certain time, so the ruling ends at it and is grasped by opinion. (He said: If the ruling is known to be dependent on a maslaha, then its disappearance is known, like the share of the reconciled, then it is the disappearance of the ruling due to the disappearance of the 'illa, as in the share of the reconciled. This is not abrogation at all, for it is the Lawgiver lifting the established ruling. This, and you may say: Specification of durations by qiyas is not pure opinion so that it would be a revealer of this indication. So this is the first principle/the book 103: grasping its ending by it, but rather by establishing a proof from the Lawgiver as previously. So they are equal, so we must return to what we said, so remember.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute on whether qiyas can act as a nasikh (abrogator) or be mansukh (abrogated). The author begins by clarifying that qiyas derived now is considered from the time of the Lawgiver; its abrogating or abrogated status is from that era, not from the present mujtahid's own judgment. If qiyas could establish a new ruling now, it would imply a gap in the complete Shariah. The author asserts that qiyas is neither abrogator nor abrogated unless the 'illa is textual and certain in the branch; then it is like a nass. Supporting this, he cites that the Companions only used opinion (ra'y) when no text existed, and never used qiyas to overturn an established ruling. He distinguishes this from qiyas used for takhsis (specification), where they used opinion as a qarina to reinterpret the apparent meaning of speculative texts. He quotes the 'Greatest Shaykh' (likely Ibn Arabi or similar) that qiyas is not an absolute proof but only a necessity. He then addresses conflicting qiyases: the earlier origin is abrogated by the later one, but this abrogation occurred in the Lawgiver's time, not now. The opponent argues that naskh is specification of duration, which is like specification of individuals, and since specification by qiyas is valid for individuals, it should be for durations. The Hanafi response denies the analogy: opinion has no role in determining the end of a ruling's duration. Even if a ruling is tied to a maslaha that disappears, that is not naskh but simply the ruling ceasing due to the disappearance of its 'illa, as in the share of those whose hearts are reconciled (sahm al-mu'allafa). Finally, the author concludes that specification of durations by qiyas is not pure opinion but requires a proof from the Lawgiver, so the earlier position stands.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): A method of legal deduction by analogy from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause ('illa).
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation, lifting it completely and replacing it with another.
المصلحة (al-maslaha): A benefit or consideration that the Lawgiver intends for humanity, which may change over time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, can qiyas act as a nasikh (abrogator) for a ruling established by a text?
A) Yes, if the 'illa is textual and certain.
B) No, never, because qiyas is only used in absence of text.
C) Yes, always, because qiyas is an independent proof.
D) Only for speculative texts, not for definitive ones.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a subordinate proof that cannot abrogate or be abrogated; only if its 'illa is textual and certain does it have the force of a text, but it never overrides an established ruling.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
10 min
Effect of Naskh on Qiyas Branch Ruling
Dispute on whether branch ruling remains when original is abrogated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions on whether a qiyasi ruling remains when its original is abrogated, and evaluate the Hanafi argument using causation analysis.

Core Idea
When the original's ruling is abrogated, does the qiyas branch stand? The dispute may be verbal.

Imagine you derive a ruling by analogy from an original case, then that original ruling is abrogated. Does your derived ruling still hold? This is a classical usul dispute. The passage presents both sides, focusing on whether the cause ('illa) remains effective after naskh. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to trace rulings back to their causes and recognize when a ruling is truly removed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue and the Two Positions
Pinpoint the core question: When the original ruling (asl) for qiyas is abrogated, does the branch ruling (far') remain? State the two contrasting answers found in the text.
Position 1: Branch does not remain (majority). Position 2: Branch remains (attributed to some Hanafis).
2
Analyze the Hanafi Position and Its Proof
The text says 'for us: abrogating the original is a nullification of the cause from causality'. Understand the Hanafi argument: if the cause is nullified, the branch that depended on it is baseless. Note the objection that the cause might be stronger in the branch.
Key concept: 'نحن' (for us) refers to the dominant Hanafi view.
3
Examine the Opposing Argument and the Hanafi Response
The opponent says: naskh of the original does not necessarily nullify the cause; the cause may remain, and the branch can stand. The Hanafi response: if the cause is stronger in the branch, it becomes delalah (textual indication), not qiyas. Also, analogy to partial naskh of a general rule is discussed.
Note the reference to Ibn Mas'ud: a general rule can be partially abrogated for some individuals while remaining for others.
4
Evaluate the Verbal Nature of the Dispute
The author suggests 'الأشبه أن النزاع لفظي' (the dispute is likely verbal). Understand what this means: the difference may be in definition (what counts as naskh) rather than in practical outcome. Consider both sides' definitions.
Verbal disputes can often be resolved by clarifying terms.
5
Determine the Practical Outcome (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Even if the dispute is verbal, the practical ruling (mufta bihi) needs to be identified. The text leans toward the branch remaining until a separate remover appears. Reflect on when a qiyasi ruling would actually be considered invalid.
The thamarah: whether a new mujtahid can rely on the qiyas after the original is abrogated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : إذا نسخ حكم الأصل للقياس (لا يبقى حكم الفرع الثابت بالقياس على هذا الأصل (وهذا ليس نسخاً عند الجمهور وقيل نسخ قالوا لأن انتفاء الحكم لانتفاء العلة ليس من النسخ فإنه رفع من الشارع ولم يوجد وأيضاً هذا انتهاء جلي، فإنه يعرف عند ملاحظة حكم الأصل، وعلته أنه يزول بزوالها فهو موجب موقت وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإن الأول إعادة عين الدعوى، والحكم قد كان ثابتاً من الشارع، وإنما أزال بإزالته وإلغاء علته، فهو رفع من الشارع وهذا هو النسخ، وزوال العلة قد يكون خفياً أيضاً، بحيث لا يعلم إلا عند إبانة الشرع انتفاء الحكم المعلل بها عند وجودها، كما فيما نحن فيه. والأشبه أن النزاع لفظي (وقيل: يبقى) حكم الفرع عند انتساخ حكم الأصل ونسب) هذا إلى الحنفية) أشار إلى هذه النسبة لم تثبت وكيف لا وقد صرحوا أن النص المنسوخ لا يصح عليه القياس وسيجيء في شروط القياس أن من شروطه أن لا يكون حكم الأصل منسوخاً لنا: أن نسخ الأصل إلغاء للعلة عن العلية وهو ظاهر فيرتفع الفرع) أي حكمه (وإلا) أي وإن لم يرتفع حكم الفرع (لكان) ثبوته (عن غير دليل ولو بقاء) إذ غير القياس مفروض الانتفاء، والقياس قد تقاعد لعدم اعتبار الشارع ،علته وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإن العلة ربما كانت في الفرع أقوى، ومن ارتفاع الأصل لا يلزم إلا عدم اعتبار قدر العلة الموجودة فيه، ولا يلزم منه عدم اعتبارها مطلقاً، فيجوز أن يبقى القدر الموجود في الفرع معتبراً، فبقى الحكم المنوط بها فيه، إلا أن يقال المناط إذا كان أقوى في الفرع يكون دلالة لا قياساً، والقياس إنما يكون فيما إذا كان الفرع مساوياً للأصل في العلة ،وأضعف وحينئذ يلزم البتة من عدم اعتبار القدر الموجود في الأصل عدم اعتبار الموجود في الفرع، لكن هذا اصطلاح محض لا يغني من الحق شيئاً، فإن مناط الفرق والقياس على كون المناط مفهوماً لغة وعدمه، فإذا لم يكن المناط مفهوماً لغة بل رأياً يعود الإشكال ،قهقرى ثم ههنا بحث آخر هو أن انتساخ الأصل لا يوجب عدم اعتبار العلة، بل يجوز أن تبقى العلة معتبرة، وإنما رفع حكم العلة بطريان مفسدة مختصة بالأصل لأجلها ارتفع، ويبقى القدر الموجود في الفرع من العلة معتبراً، سواء كان مساوياً لما في الأصل أو أضعف، ويبقى الحكم لوجود العلة وانتفاء المفسدة من الحكم ومما يؤيد ما قلنا إن نسخ الحكم عن بعض أفراد العام مع بقائه في البعض جائز من غير ريبة كما صح عن ابن مسعود، فقد انتفى اعتبار العلة في البعض إما بإلغاء القدر الموجود فيه وإما لغلبة مفسدة مختصة به مع أنه لم ينتف اعتبار العلة في البعض الآخر، حتى بقي الحكم فليكن فيما نحن فيه كذلك فتأمل فيه. قائلو بقاء حكم الفرع مع انتفاء حكم الأصل (قالوا : أولاً : الفرع تابع للدلالة للأصل على الحكم (وهي باقية لا لحكم الأصل وهو المنتفى فقط، والدلالة باقية كما كانت فيبقى تابعها (قلنا) حكم الفرع إنما تبع لدلالة الأصل بوساطة العلة المعتبرة شرعاً، وإذا نسخ الأصل لزم من انتفاء الأصل انتفاء الحكمة المعتبرة شرعاً) فانتفى التابع وأيضاً تعلق حكم الفرع بذمة المكلف تابع لتعلق حكم الأصل، وقد زال التعلق فقد زال تابعه ولك أن تقول : إن الموجب للحكم العلة والنص كان يدل عليه بوساطة العلة، فالحكم الشرعي المستفاد من العلة إنما فهم من النص بالتبعية والحكم من الشارع لا يرتفع إلا بظهور رافع، والرافع إما ناسخ فهو لم يرفع إلا حكم الأصل فقط، وأما عدم اعتبار العلة والحكمة المعتبرة فيها فكلا، ولم يظهر عدم الاعتبار من انتساخ الأصل كما قررنا، فلا بد من بقاء الحكم إلى ظهور عدم اعتباره لدليل منفصل، أو ظهور ناسخ آخر فعليك بالتأمل الصادق (و) قالوا (ثانياً) لو استلزم انتساخ حكم الأصل انتفاء حكم الفرع فليس إلا لقياس الانتفاء على الانتفاء ورفع حكم الفرع قياساً على رفع حكم الأصل من غير جامع، قلنا لا نسلم الملازمة فإن مناط انتفاء حكم الفرع ليس هو القياس (بل) إنما ينتفي بانتفاء العلة الموجبة للحكم المعلوم بانتفاء حكم الأصل) بالنسخ، ولك أن تقول : إنّ انتفاء العلة الموجبة للحكم مطلقاً من الأصل والفرع لم يظهر، فلو ارتفع عن الفرع لارتفع بقياس ارتفاع حكم الفرع على ارتفاعه في الأصل، وهو قياس من غير جامع، فعليك بالتأمل الصادق فتأمل.
Issue: When the ruling of the original for qiyas is abrogated, the ruling of the branch established by qiyas on this original does not remain. This is not abrogation according to the majority, and it is said [to be] abrogation. They said because the negation of the ruling due to the negation of the cause is not abrogation, for it is a removal from the Lawgiver that did not occur. Also, this is a clear termination, for it is known upon observing the ruling of the original and its cause that it ceases with its cessation, so it is a temporary obligation. There is an apparent flaw in this, for the first is a restatement of the very claim, and the ruling had been established from the Lawgiver, and He only removed it by removing its cause and canceling its cause-effect relation, so it is a removal from the Lawgiver and that is abrogation. The cessation of the cause may also be hidden, such that it is not known except when the Law indicates the negation of the ruling that is caused by it when it exists, as in our case. The more likely [view] is that the dispute is verbal. And it is said: the ruling of the branch remains when the ruling of the original is abrogated, and this is attributed to the Hanafis. He indicated that this attribution is not established, and how not? They have explicitly stated that the abrogated text is not valid for qiyas, and it will come in the conditions of qiyas that among its conditions is that the ruling of the original not be abrogated. For us: abrogating the original is a nullification of the cause from causality, which is apparent, so the branch (i.e., its ruling) is removed. Otherwise (i.e., if the branch ruling is not removed), its existence would be without evidence, even if [it exists] as a continuation, since other than qiyas is assumed absent, and qiyas has become ineffective due to the Lawgiver's disregard of its cause. There is an apparent flaw in this, for the cause may be stronger in the branch, and from the removal of the original it does not follow except the disregard of the amount of cause present in it, and it does not entail its disregard absolutely; it is permissible that the amount present in the branch remains considered, so the ruling contingent upon it remains. Unless it is said that if the manat is stronger in the branch, it becomes a [textual] indication, not qiyas. Qiyas only applies when the branch equals the original in cause or is weaker. In that case it necessarily follows from the disregard of the amount present in the original the disregard of the amount present in the branch. But this is a mere convention that does not substitute for truth. For the criterion of distinction and qiyas depends on whether the manat is understood linguistically or not. If the manat is not understood linguistically but is a matter of opinion, the problem returns back. Then here is another investigation: abrogation of the original does not necessitate disregard of the cause; rather, the cause may remain considered, and only the ruling of the cause was removed due to a specific harm pertaining to the original, for which it was removed. The amount of cause present in the branch remains considered, whether equal to that in the original or weaker, and the ruling remains due to the existence of the cause and the absence of harm in the ruling. Supporting what we said is that abrogation of the ruling from some individuals of the general while it remains in others is permissible without doubt, as narrated from Ibn Mas'ud. Thus, the disregard of the cause occurred in some individuals either by canceling the amount present in them or due to a specific harm pertaining to them, while disregard of the cause did not occur in other individuals, so the ruling remained. Let it be similar in our case, so reflect. Those who say the branch ruling remains while the original's ruling is removed said: First, the branch follows the indication of the original to the ruling, which remains, not the ruling of the original, which alone is removed. The indication remains as it was, so its follower remains. We say: The ruling of the branch only follows the indication of the original through the cause considered legally. When the original is abrogated, the removal of the original necessitates the removal of the legally considered wisdom, so the follower is removed. Also, the attachment of the branch ruling to the Mukallaf's liability follows the attachment of the original ruling; that attachment has ceased, so its follower has ceased. But you could say: The obligator of the ruling is the cause, and the text indicated it through the cause. The legal ruling derived from the cause is understood from the text as a follow-on. The ruling from the Lawgiver is not removed except by the appearance of a remover. The remover is either an abrogator, which removed only the original ruling. As for the disregard of the cause and the wisdom considered in it, it is not so, and disregard has not appeared from the abrogation of the original as we have established. So the ruling must remain until the appearance of its disregard through a separate evidence, or the appearance of another abrogator. So be honest in reflection. They said, second: If the abrogation of the original ruling necessarily entailed the negation of the branch ruling, that would only be by analogizing negation to negation and removing the branch ruling by qiyas on the removal of the original ruling without a common factor. We say: We do not accept the entailment, for the criterion for the negation of the branch ruling is not qiyas; rather, it is negated by the negation of the cause that obligates the ruling, which is known from the negation of the original ruling through abrogation. But you could say: The negation of the cause that obligates the ruling absolutely from both original and branch has not appeared. If it were removed from the branch, it would be removed by analogizing the removal of the branch ruling to its removal in the original, which is qiyas without a common factor. So be honest in reflection.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage discusses a key usul debate: when the ruling of an original (asl) is abrogated (naskh), what happens to the ruling of a branch (far') that was established by qiyas on that original? The text presents multiple positions. The majority view holds that the branch ruling does not remain because the cause ('illa) is eliminated, making it a natural termination, not abrogation. However, some say it is abrogation because the Lawgiver removes the ruling via removing the cause. The author notes the dispute may be verbal. Importantly, the Hanafi position cited is that the branch ruling does not remain, as the cause is considered null. The commentary examines arguments: if the cause were stronger in the branch, it might remain, but this would be delalah, not qiyas. The analogy to partial abrogation of a general rule (as per Ibn Mas'ud) supports the possibility of the branch remaining. Ultimately, the author favors the view that the branch ruling remains until a separate evidence of removal appears, emphasizing careful reflection.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by the Lawgiver
علة ('illa): The effective cause that justifies a ruling in qiyas
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from an original to a branch based on a common cause
دلالة (delalah): Textual indication; a stronger proof than qiyas when the cause is explicitly stated
مناط (manat): The basis or relevant attribute on which a ruling is grounded

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the most likely nature of the dispute regarding the branch ruling upon abrogation of the original?
A) It is a real dispute about the definition of naskh
B) It is a verbal dispute
C) It is a purely rational dispute
D) It is a dispute about conditions of qiyas

Key Takeaway
The ruling of a qiyas branch may remain after the original is abrogated if the cause remains effective; the dispute is often verbal and requires careful reflection.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
