Dispute on Increase of Parts or Conditions as Naskh (Hanafi vs Others)
Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on whether adding a part or condition constitutes abrogation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that increasing a part or condition constitutes naskh, identify the opposing views, and apply the nuanced criteria of whether the addition changes the essence of the obligation.

Core Idea
Adding a part or condition is naskh if it changes the essence of the obligation, requiring restart.

This passage tackles a foundational usul dispute: does adding a new requirement (like a rak'a in prayer or a condition in expiation) abrogate the original obligation? The Hanafis say yes, calling it naskh bil-ziyada, while Shafi'is and others disagree. We will examine the arguments, including a middle position that distinguishes between changes that alter the essence and those that do not, and critique a common error.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its definition
Recognize that Hanafis consider any increase in a part or condition as naskh (naskh bil-ziyada) because it changes the original obligation.
e.g., adding two rak'as to a two-rak'a prayer abrogates the original two-rak'a obligation.
2
Identify the opposing view and its rationale
Shafi'is, Hanbalis, and most Mu'tazila deny that increase constitutes naskh, arguing it adds a new requirement without nullifying the original.
They see it as supplement rather than abrogation.
3
Examine Abd al-Jabbar's intermediate position
Abd al-Jabbar distinguishes: if the addition changes the essence so that performing the original alone is invalid (like adding a rak'a), it is naskh; if not (like adding stoning to flogging), it is not.
This focuses on functional impact.
4
Critique Ibn al-Hajib's error
Ibn al-Hajib erroneously equated adding stoning (which does not require restart of flogging) to cases that do require restart; the text corrects this by noting flogging becomes legally ineffective with stoning added.
The critique uses a definition of 'change' as making the original act legally non-existent.
5
Evaluate the final opinion by Imam al-Haramayn et al.
They hold that it depends on whether the addition removes a legal ruling; if yes, it is naskh; otherwise not. This is a case-by-case approach.
This reconciles the extremes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما زيادة جزء) في الواجب كالتغريب في الحد) أي حد الزنا (أو) زيادة (شرط) بعد إطلاق الواجب عنه (كالإيمان) أي اشتراطه في رقبة اليمين فهل هو نسخ لحكم المزيد عليه (فالحنفية) قالوا: (نعم) نسخ، وهو المسمى عندهم بالنسخ بالزيادة والشافعية والحنابلة وأكثر المعتزلة قالوا : (لا) نسخ ( وعبد الجبار من المعتزلة قال : (إن غير هذا الجزء أو الشرط أصل الواجب المزيد حتى لو فعل) المكلف إياه كما كان قبل الزيادة (وجب استئنافه كزيادة ركعة كما روى الشيخان عن أم المؤمنين أن الصلاة الرباعية كانت اثنتين ثم زيد ،ركعتان والآن لو صلّى الظهر ركعتين لم يجز ووجب الاستئناف (أو) كان ( كتخيير) معطوف على غير لا على قوله كزيادة ركعة كما لا يخفى (في ثلاث من الخصال (بعده) أي بعد التخيير الثابت في ثنتين) فإنه رافع لحرمة ترك الاثنتين إلى إباحته بشرط الإتيان بالثالث (فنسخ) أي فالزيادة نسخ (بخلاف زيادة التغريب على الحد الذي هو الجلد فإنه لا جلد ولم يغرّب لا يجب استئناف الجلد وغلط هنا ابن الحاجب) حيث جعل زيادة التغريب نظيراً لما غَيَّر، ولعل بناء كلامه على أنه فسر التغيير بأن يكون وجوده على ما كان كالعدم بحيث لا يعتد شرعاً، ولا يكون ممتثلاً به، ولا شك أن الجلد على تقدير زيادة التغريب كذلك، فتغليطه إنما هو بناء على تفسير المصنف إذا صح النقل لكنهم يرجحونه بأنه نقل الآمدي وهو ثقة في الباب والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال (وقيل: إن رفع هذا الجزء أو الشرط حكماً شرعياً (فنسخ وإلا لا واختاره الإمام) إمام الحرمين (و) الإمام الرازي) والآمدي كلهم من الشافعية (أقول : مرادهم أنه لا يضبط) الأمر (كلياً لا نفياً ولا إثباتاً بل في بعض الأحكام يكون رافعاً لحكم شرعي، فيكون نسخاً، وفي الآخر لا، فلا يكون فاندفع ما في التنقيح أنه كلام خال عن التحصيل لأن كل أحد يعترف به) وإنما الخلاف في أنه رافع أم لا، ووجه الاندافع ظاهر، قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية والدي قدس سره: هكذا نقل في شرح الشرح ، وليس في التنقيح ذكره أصلاً إلا أن يكون هذا التنقيح غير التنقيح
And as for increase of a part in an obligatory act, like stoning in the hadd, i.e., the hadd of zina, or increase of a condition after the obligation was unrestricted from it, like faith, i.e., stipulating it in the expiation slave, is it naskh for the ruling of the increased upon? The Hanafis said: yes, it is naskh, and it is called by them naskh by increase. The Shafi'is, Hanbalis, and most Mu'tazila said: no, it is not naskh. And Abd al-Jabbar of the Mu'tazila said: this part or condition changes the essence of the obligatory act increased, such that if the mukallaf does it as it was before the increase, he must restart it, like the increase of a rak'a, as the two Shaykhs narrated from the Mother of the Believers that the four-rak'a prayer was two, then two rak'as were added, and now if one prays Dhuhr with two rak'as, it is not permissible and he must restart. Or it is like a choice, conjoined to 'change' not to 'increase of a rak'a' as is clear, in three of the characteristics after the choice established in two; for it removes the prohibition of leaving the two to its permissibility with the condition of performing the third, so the increase is naskh. Unlike the increase of stoning upon the hadd which is flogging, for if he flogs and does not stone, restart of flogging is not required. And here Ibn al-Hajib erred in making increase of stoning analogous to what changes, perhaps his statement is based on his interpretation of 'change' as being such that its existence is like non-existence so that it is not legally considered, and he is not complying with it. There is no doubt that flogging upon the assumption of increase of stoning is like that, so his correction is based on the author's interpretation if the transmission is correct, but they give preference to it because it is transmitted by al-Amidi who is reliable in the subject, and Allah knows best the true situation. And it was said: if this part or condition removes a legal ruling, then it is naskh, otherwise not, and this was chosen by Imam al-Haramayn, Imam al-Razi, and al-Amidi, all from the Shafi'is. I say: their meaning is that it is not to be regulated universally, neither by negation nor affirmation, but rather in some rulings it removes a legal ruling, thus it is naskh, and in others not, thus it is not naskh. So what is in al-Tanqih that it is speech devoid of investigation is repelled, because everyone acknowledges it; the dispute is only whether it is remover or not, and the aspect of repulsion is apparent. The author of Matla' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya, my father, may Allah sanctify his secret, said: thus it is transmitted in Sharh al-Sharh, and it is not mentioned in al-Tanqih at all, unless this al-Tanqih is other than al-Tanqih.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage addresses whether adding a part (juz') or condition (shart) to an obligatory act constitutes naskh. The Hanafi position is clear: yes, it is naskh, specifically termed 'naskh by increase' (naskh bil-ziyada). The Shafi'is, Hanbalis, and most Mu'tazila say no. A middle position by Abd al-Jabbar distinguishes cases: if the addition changes the essence so that performing the original act alone is invalid and requires restart (like adding raka'at to prayer), it is naskh; if not (like adding stoning to flogging), it is not. Ibn al-Hajib's error is discussed for equating the addition of stoning to cases of change. Finally, a third opinion by Imam al-Haramayn, al-Razi, and al-Amidi holds that it depends on whether the addition removes a legal ruling—if yes, it is naskh; if no, it is not. The passage concludes with a note about al-Tanqih and its attribution.

Key Terms
زيادة جزء (ziyadat juz'): Adding a part to an obligatory act (e.g., a rak'a or stoning in hadd).
نسخ بالزيادة (naskh bil-ziyada): Abrogation by increase; the Hanafi term for when an addition changes the original obligation.
تغريب (taghrib): Banishment; added as a punishment for zina along with flogging.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following additions does the Hanafi school consider as naskh?
A) Adding stoning to flogging for zina
B) Adding the condition of faith to the expiation slave
C) Adding two rak'as to a two-rak'a prayer
D) Adding banishment to flogging

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position that increase in parts or conditions constitutes naskh rests on whether the addition changes the nature of the obligation, making the original act invalid without it.

Removal of the Description of Being Middle is Not Abrogation
Analyzing whether a change in a prayer's description constitutes naskh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a rational description (waṣf ʿaqlī) from a legal ruling (ḥukm sharʿī) and apply this distinction to evaluate whether adding a sixth prayer via khabar wāḥid constitutes naskh.

Core Idea
A rational description like 'middle' is not part of the legal ruling; its removal does not abrogate the obligation.

This lesson tackles a subtle question in uṣūl al-fiqh: does a change in a prayer's description amount to abrogation of its obligation? The debate arises from the Hanafi ruling that Witr is wājib even though it adds a sixth daily prayer, potentially conflicting with the definitively established obligation of the 'middle prayer' (al-ṣalāt al-wusṭā). The passage defends the Hanafi view by analyzing the nature of the description 'middle' — it is a rational attribute, not a legal ruling. Understanding this distinction is key to preserving the integrity of qaṭʿī rulings when dealing with ẓannī evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
The passage addresses whether adding a sixth obligatory prayer (Witr) via a single-transmitter hadith (khabar wāḥid) abrogates the definitively established obligation to preserve the middle prayer. The opponent argues that losing the description 'middle' destroys the obligation.
The obligation of the middle prayer is qaṭʿī; Witr's proof is ẓannī.
2
Examine the Opponent's Argument
The opponent claims that rulings on derived terms (mushtaqqāt) are tied to the root meaning. Thus, the obligation is for a prayer described as 'middle'; if that description vanishes, the obligation vanishes.
This argument treats the description as integral to the ruling.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis respond that the description 'middle' is a rational attribute (waṣf ʿaqlī), not a legal ruling. The ruling is the obligation of the prayer itself, independent of this accidental quality. Hence, losing the description does not nullify the obligation.
Rational descriptions do not affect the ḥukm sharʿī.
4
Evaluate the Counter-Objection
The opponent further insists that derived-term rulings require the root meaning. The Hanafis concede the appearance but assert that the actual legislative intent is the prayer itself, not the description. Being middle has no bearing on the obligation; the obligation attaches to the act (prayer) qua prayer.
The response upholds that the ruling is on the entity, not the accident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإمام وصاحبيه صلاة العصر، وهو مذهب أكثر الصحابة والتابعين والأحاديث وإن كانت متعارضة لكن القوة لأحاديث العصر، والتفصيل في فتح المنان في تأييد مذهب النعمان للشيخ عبد الحق الدهلوي رحمه الله تعالى وفائدة هذا القول تظهر في إيجاب صلاة الوتر بخبر الواحد، فإنه لما كان إيجاب السادسة نسخاً عندهم لإيجاب المحافظة على الوسطى الثابت بالقاطع لم يكن إيجاب الوتر بخبر الواحد صحيحاً، وإلا لزم انتساخ القاطع بالمظنون وحله أن الوصف) وصف التوسط (عقلي) لا حكم شرعي، بل الحكم هو إيجاب الموصوف بهذا الوصف، والزائل هو وصف التوسط (ولا) (يلزم من زواله بطلان الموصوف) أي بطلان إيجاب الموصوف، ولعل مطمح نظر هذا البعض أن الأحكام المتعلقة بالمشتقات تتقيد بإنصاف المبدأ، فالمعنى: إيجاب الصلاة الموصوفة بهذا الوصف أي إيقاعها على وجه تكون متوسطة، ولا شك أن إيجاب السادسة يبطل هذا الحكم لكنا نقول: هب أن الظاهر في الأحكام المتعلقة بالمشتقات ما ذكرتم، إلا أنه لا شك أن الغرض ههنا إيجاب نفس الصلاة المعنونة بها، ولا دخل لكونها وسطى في الإيجاب فتأمل فيه
Imam and his two companions (say) the 'Asr prayer, and it is the madhhab of most Companions and Followers, and the hadiths although conflicting, but the strength is for the hadiths of 'Asr, and the detail is in Fath al-Mannan fi Ta'yid Madhhab al-Nu'man by Shaykh Abd al-Haqq al-Dahlawi (may Allah have mercy on him). The benefit of this statement appears in making the Witr prayer obligatory by a khabar wahid, because when making the sixth (prayer) was abrogation in their view of the obligation of preserving the middle (prayer) established by a definitive text, making Witr obligatory by a khabar wahid is not valid, otherwise it would entail abrogation of the definitive by the conjectural. Its solution is that the description (the description of being middle) is rational, not a legal ruling. Rather the ruling is the obligation of the described with this description, and what vanishes is the description of being middle, and the annihilation of the described (i.e., the annulment of the obligation of the described) does not follow from its annihilation. Perhaps the aim of this person is that the rulings related to derived terms are restricted to the occurrence of the principle, so the meaning is: the obligation of prayer described with this description, i.e., performing it in a way that it is middle, and there is no doubt that the obligation of the sixth nullifies this ruling. But we say: even if it is apparent in rulings related to derived terms what you mentioned, there is no doubt that the purpose here is the obligation of the prayer itself designated by it, and being middle has no bearing on the obligation, so reflect on it.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific issue: whether adding a sixth prayer (Witr) via a single-transmitter hadith (khabar wahid) constitutes abrogation (naskh) of the established obligation to preserve the 'middle prayer' (al-salāt al-wusṭā). The author rejects that view by analyzing that the description of being 'middle' is a rational attribute, not a legal ruling (ḥukm sharʿī). The legal ruling is simply the obligation of the prayer itself, not the description. Hence, losing the description does not invalidate the obligation's continuity. The passage responds to an unnamed objector who argued that rulings on derived terms (mushtaqqāt) are tied to the root meaning; the author counters that the actual intent is the prayer itself, independent of the description.

Key Terms
الوصف العقلي (al-waṣf al-ʿaqlī): A description that is purely rational (ʿaqlī) not a legal ruling, such as 'middle' (tawassuṭ).
الوسطى (al-wusṭā): The middle prayer, specifically the ʿAṣr prayer according to the author's preferred view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the description is a legal ruling that can be changed without abrogation.
B) Because the description is rational, not a legal ruling, and the obligation remains on the act itself.
C) Because the obligation was originally for six prayers and the middle prayer is no longer required.
D) Because the hadith establishing the description is stronger than the proof for the obligation.

Key Takeaway
A rational description (waṣf ʿaqlī) of an act is not part of the legal ruling; its removal does not constitute abrogation (naskh) of the obligation.

Naskh — Abrogation

Adding a Part or Condition as Abrogation: The Hanafi Position
Dispute over whether adding a part/condition constitutes naskh, with illustrative examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis consider adding a part or condition to an obligation as abrogation (naskh bi al-ziyada) and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i argument using examples from prayer and hadd punishments.

Core Idea
Adding a part or condition removes the permissibility of doing without it, thus abrogating the original mutlaq ruling.

This passage presents a key usul dispute: does adding a new requirement (part or condition) to an originally unrestricted obligation constitute abrogation (naskh)? The Hanafis affirm it, while the Shafi'is, Hanbalis, and most Mu'tazila deny it. The discussion uses concrete examples — adding a rak'ah to prayer and adding stoning to flogging — to illustrate the practical consequences and refine the definition of 'change' that triggers naskh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and its scope
Recognize that the core issue is whether adding a part (juz') or condition (shart) to a formerly unrestricted (mutlaq) obligation constitutes naskh. Note the two main camps: Hanafis vs. Shafi'is/Hanbalis/Mu'tazila.
The term 'naskh bi al-ziyada' is specific to Hanafis.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof and its foundation
Understand the Hanafi argument: the original mutlaq text implied permissibility of the act without the addition; adding a part/condition removes that permissibility, which is the essence of naskh (lifting a shar'i ruling).
Key concept: mutlaq implies permissibility of any instance.
3
Examine the opposing position and its counter-proof
The Shafi'is argue that the addition merely supplements; the original ruling remains valid. They deny that permissibility is lifted, because the original text is not repealed but complemented.
Opponents see naskh only when the original ruling is completely removed.
4
Differentiate the two examples: prayer vs. hadd
The Hanafis use the prayer example (adding two rak'ahs) as a clear case of naskh: the original two-rak'ah prayer is no longer valid. In contrast, adding stoning to flogging does not abrogate flogging; if one only flogs, it suffices. The difference lies in whether the original act becomes legally disregarded.
Ibn al-Hajib's error: he analogized the hadd case to the prayer case, but the Hanafis argue they differ.
5
Conclude with the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a person performs the original obligation without the added part, Hanafis require repetition (istinaf); Shafi'is do not. This difference affects millions of daily acts like expiations and punishments.
The example of freeing a believing slave in kaffara: Hanafi view requires a believing slave; Shafi'i view allows any slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما زيادة جزء) في الواجب كالتغريب في الحد) أي حد الزنا (أو) زيادة (شرط) بعد إطلاق الواجب عنه (كالإيمان) أي اشتراطه في رقبة اليمين فهل هو نسخ لحكم المزيد عليه (فالحنفية) قالوا: (نعم) نسخ، وهو المسمى عندهم بالنسخ بالزيادة والشافعية والحنابلة وأكثر المعتزلة قالوا : (لا) نسخ ( وعبد الجبار من المعتزلة قال : (إن غير هذا الجزء أو الشرط أصل الواجب المزيد حتى لو فعل) المكلف إياه كما كان قبل الزيادة (وجب استئنافه كزيادة ركعة كما روى الشيخان عن أم المؤمنين أن الصلاة الرباعية كانت اثنتين ثم زيد ركعتان والآن لو صلّى الظهر ركعتين لم يجز ووجب الاستئناف (أو) كان ( كتخيير) معطوف على غير لا على قوله كزيادة ركعة كما لا يخفى (في ثلاث من الخصال (بعده) أي بعد التخيير الثابت في ثنتين) فإنه رافع لحرمة ترك الاثنتين إلى إباحته بشرط الإتيان بالثالث (فنسخ) أي فالزيادة نسخ (بخلاف زيادة التغريب على الحد الذي هو الجلد فإنه لا جلد ولم يغرّب لا يجب استئناف الجلد وغلط هنا ابن الحاجب) حيث جعل زيادة التغريب نظيراً لما غَيَّر، ولعل بناء كلامه على أنه فسر التغيير بأن يكون وجوده على ما كان كالعدم بحيث لا يعتد شرعاً، ولا يكون ممتثلاً به، ولا شك أن الجلد على تقدير زيادة التغريب كذلك، فتغليطه إنما هو بناء على تفسير المصنف إذا صح النقل لكنهم يرجحونه بأنه نقل الآمدي وهو ثقة في الباب والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال
As for adding a part to the obligatory, like adding stoning to the hadd (i.e., the hadd of zina), or adding a condition after the obligation was unrestricted from it, like faith (i.e., stipulating it in the expiation slave), then is it abrogation of the ruling of the original? The Hanafis said: Yes, it is abrogation, and it is called among them abrogation by addition. The Shafi'is, Hanbalis, and most Mu'tazila said: It is not abrogation. And 'Abd al-Jabbar from the Mu'tazila said: If this part or condition changes the essence of the increased obligation such that if the mukallaf does it as before the increase, he must restart, like adding a rak'ah as narrated by the two shaykhs from Umm al-Mu'minin that the four-rak'ah prayer was two, then two rak'ahs were added, and now if one prays Zuhr two rak'ahs, it is not valid and he must restart. Or (if the addition) is like giving a choice among three characteristics after the choice established in two, for it removes the prohibition of leaving the two to its permissibility with the condition of performing the third, so it is abrogation (i.e., the addition is abrogation). Unlike adding stoning to the hadd which is flogging: if he flogs and does not stone, it is not obligatory to restart flogging. Ibn al-Hajib erred here by making adding stoning analogous to that which changes. Perhaps his statement is based on his interpretation that change means that its existence after the change is like non-existence such that it is legally disregarded and not complied with, and there is no doubt that flogging on the assumption of adding stoning is like that. So his correction is based on the author's interpretation if the transmission is correct, but they prefer it because it is transmitted by al-Amidi who is trustworthy in this field, and Allah knows the reality of the situation.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position that adding a part (juz') or condition (shart) to an obligatory act constitutes abrogation (naskh) of the original obligation. The opposing schools (Shafi'i, Hanbali, most Mu'tazila) deny it. 'Abd al-Jabbar differentiates: if the addition changes the essence so the original performance becomes invalid (e.g., adding rak'ahs to prayer), it is abrogation; if it is like adding a choice among three options after two, it is also abrogation. However, adding stoning to flogging does not require restarting flogging if only flogging is done. The author critiques Ibn al-Hajib for wrongly analogizing stoning addition to changes that nullify the original.

Key Terms
النسخ بالزيادة (al-naskh bi al-ziyāda): The abrogation that occurs by adding a part or condition to an existing ruling, according to Hanafis.
التغريب (al-taghrīb): Exile or stoning as an additional punishment in zinā hadd.
مطلق (mutlaq): An unrestricted expression that applies to any instance of its genus without qualification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafis, if a condition (like faith in expiation slave) is added to an originally unrestricted obligation, this is:
A) Not considered abrogation.
B) Considered abrogation by addition (naskh bi al-ziyada).
C) Considered only a recommended practice.
D) Considered abrogation only if the condition invalidates the original act.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers adding a part or condition to a mutlaq obligation as abrogation (naskh bi al-ziyada), requiring the act to be performed with the addition for validity.

Addition as Naskh: Universal Rule or Contextual?
Juwayni, Razi, and Amidi reject blanket naskh ruling for additions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on addition as naskh and analyse the Shafi'i counter-argument from Juwayni, Razi, and Amidi.

Core Idea
Addition always naskh? Juwayni, Razi, Amidi say: only if it removes a shar‘i ruling.

In usul al-fiqh, one of the key disputes is whether adding a new part or condition to a legal obligation always abrogates (naskh) the previous ruling. The Hanafi school holds that any addition necessarily raises the original mutlaq ruling, making it naskh. However, leading Shafi'i scholars al-Juwayni, al-Razi, and al-Amidi reject this blanket rule. This lesson unpacks their nuanced view and the underlying reasoning, helping you see how the same textual evidence can yield divergent usul rules.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi rule on addition as naskh
Recall the Hanafi position: any addition of a part or condition to a legal obligation is considered naskh (abrogation) of the previous ruling. This is based on the principle that the original ruling was absolute (mutlaq) and the addition restricts or qualifies it.
This rule is part of the Hanafi definition of naskh.
2
Identify the opposing view of Juwayni, Razi, and Amidi
These Shafi'i scholars argue that there is no universal rule. Addition only constitutes naskh if it actually raises (removes) a prior shar'i ruling. If the addition merely clarifies or complements without nullifying the original, it is not naskh.
They focus on the effect of the addition on the previous ruling.
3
Analyse the opposing dalil
Their evidence is based on textual examples where the Prophet (SAW) added conditions to acts of worship. They argue that some additions do not invalidate the prior practice, so they cannot be called naskh.
Refer to the passage: 'If this part or condition raises a shar'i ruling, then it is naskh; otherwise not.'
4
Examine the Hanafi response as implied in the passage
The author defends the nuanced view, noting that the Hanafi position automatically treats any addition as raising the previous ruling because the original mutlaq ruling is replaced. The dispute is thus about whether the addition is legally effective in altering the prior ruling.
The author argues that the critique from al-Tanqih misses this point.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If addition is always naskh, then the original act performed without the addition is invalid and must be repeated. If not always naskh, the original act may remain valid even if the addition is omitted.
For example, adding a condition in prayer: Hanafis require repetition; Shafi'is may not if the addition does not remove the original obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل: إن رفع هذا الجزء أو الشرط حكماً شرعياً فنسخ وإلا لا واختاره الإمام) إمام الحرمين (و) الإمام الرازي) والآمدي كلهم من الشافعية (أقول : مرادهم أنه لا يضبط) الأمر (كلياً لا نفياً ولا إثباتاً بل في بعض الأحكام يكون رافعاً لحكم شرعي، فيكون نسخاً، وفي الآخر لا، فلا يكون فاندفع ما في التنقيح أنه كلام خال عن التحصيل لأن كل أحد يعترف به) وإنما الخلاف في أنه رافع أم لا، ووجه الاندافع ظاهر، قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية والدي قدس سره: هكذا نقل في شرح الشرح ، وليس في التنقيح ذكره أصلاً إلا أن يكون هذا التنقيح غير التنقيح المشهور. فافهم
And it was said: If this part or condition raises a shar'i ruling, then it is naskh; otherwise not. And this was chosen by Imam al-Haramayn, Imam al-Razi, and al-Amidi, all from the Shafi'is. I say: Their intent is that the matter cannot be captured universally, neither negation nor affirmation. Rather in some rulings it causes a shar'i ruling to be raised, so it is naskh; in others it does not, so it is not. Thus what is in al-Tanqih that it is speech devoid of attainment is refuted, because everyone acknowledges it. The disagreement is only whether it raises or not, and the manner of refutation is apparent. The opener of divine secrets, my father (may his secret be sanctified), said: Thus it is transmitted in Sharh al-Sharh, and there is no mention of it at all in al-Tanqih, unless this al-Tanqih is other than the famous al-Tanqih. So understand.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage presents a middle position by Imams al-Juwayni (al-Haramayn), al-Razi, and al-Amidi, all Shafi'is. They reject a blanket rule: whether adding a part or condition constitutes naskh depends on whether it raises (removes) a shar'i ruling. For example, if it allows the original act to be performed without the addition but still be valid, it is not naskh; if it invalidates the original act (requires restart), it is naskh. The author defends this view against a critique in al-Tanqih, clarifying that the critique misses the point because the real issue is whether the addition is legally effective or not.

Key Terms
رفع حكم شرعي (rafʿ ḥukm sharʿī): The removal or abrogation of a legal ruling by a later text.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a previous legal ruling by a later evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever any part is added.
B) Only when the addition removes a shar'i ruling.
C) Never, since additions merely clarify.
D) Only if the addition is mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over whether addition always constitutes naskh turns on whether the addition removes a prior shar’i ruling.

Naskh — Abrogation

Hanafi Proof: Absolute Implies Sufficiency; Addition is Naskh
Proof that adding a part/condition abrogates the absolute ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a mutlaq command indicates sufficiency and identify when adding a condition constitutes naskh, using the tawaf case as an example.

Core Idea
A mutlaq command covers all instances; adding a part/condition abrogates that sufficiency — only a qat'i text can override another qat'i.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defends its rule that an absolute Quranic command (mutlaq) is sufficient for all its individuals. They argue that adding a condition or part by a zanni (conjectural) proof would effectively abrogate the qat'i (certain) Quranic text, which is impermissible. The tawaf example illustrates this: the Quran commands tawaf absolutely, so the hadith comparing tawaf to prayer cannot impose wudu as a condition for validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the absolute text (mutlaq)
Find the Quranic verse commanding tawaf without any conditions. The verse (22:29) says 'and let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House.' It does not mention purity.
This verse is the mutlaq proof.
2
Apply the Hanafi rule: mutlaq indicates sufficiency
The absolute command covers all its individuals, including those without any added condition. Thus tawaf is valid without wudu.
The rule: al-mutlaq yufidu al-ijza' mutlaqan.
3
Recognize the addition (ziyada) as potential naskh
The hadith 'tawaf is like prayer' adds a condition of purity. In Hanafi usul, adding a part or condition to a mutlaq ruling is considered naskh (abrogation) because it removes the sufficiency of the unrestricted instance.
Naskh requires equal or stronger authority; a zanni hadith cannot abrogate a qat'i text.
4
Assess authority: qat'i vs zanni
The Quran is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) and qat'i al-dalalah (clear meaning) regarding the obligation of tawaf. The hadith is zanni (single transmission). Naskh would require both texts to be of equal certainty.
Zanni cannot abrogate qat'i.
5
Derive the Hanafi ruling
Since the hadith cannot abrogate the mutlaq, tawaf without wudu remains valid. However, out of caution, purity is considered wajib based on the hadith, and its omission requires a blood sacrifice (dam jābir) but does not invalidate the tawaf.
The mufta bihi position: tawaf without wudu is sahih but with compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لنا) أن (المطلق) عن تلك الزيادة (دل على الأجزاء مطلقاً) سواء كان مع الزيادة أو مجرداً عنها (لأنه) أي المطلق (كالعام) يدل على أفراده التي مع الزيادة أو مجرداً عنها (بدلاً) وليس هناك صارف عنه، لأن الكلام فيما لا صارف غير هذه الزيادة، وهي مفروضة الانتفاء زمان وجود المطلق فيحمل على الإطلاق، ويدل عليه (والتقييد) بجزء أو شرط (ينافيه) فإنه يقتضي عدم الإجزاء بدونه (فيرفع هذا التقييد حكماً شرعياً) وهو إجزاء الأفراد التي هي مجردة عن هذا التقييد، وهذا ظاهر جداً، ثم فرع على هذه المسألة مسألة أخرى فقال (ولهذا) ولأجل أن زيادة جزء أو شرط نسخ امتنع عندنا الزيادة بخبر الواحد على القاطع) كالكتاب، وإلا لزم انتساخ القاطع بالمظنون، فإن قلت : قد جوزتم الزيادة بالخبر المشهور مع أنه مظنون، قلت : سنبيّن وجهه إن شاء الله تعالى كالطهارة (للطواف فإنا لا نجعلها شرطاً حتى يجزىء الطواف من غير طهارة، ولا تجب الإعادة خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله تمسك أصحابه بما روى الترمذي والنسائي عن ابن عباس قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : الطواف حول البيت مثل الصلاة إلا أنكم تتكلمون فيه، فمن تكلم فيه فلا يتكلم إلاّ بخير وأجاب مشايخنا كما أشار إليه المصنف بأن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَطَوَّفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ [الحج : ٢٩] مطلق، فزيادة الطهارة عليه وتقييد إطلاقها لا يجوز بهذا الخبر المظنون بل يبقى الطواف المفروض مطلقاً، لكن قلنا بوجوب الطهارة عملاً بهذا الخبر، فيجب الدم الجابر إن طاف محدثاً، لكن سقط الفرض كذا قالوا واعترض عليه الشيخ الهداد بأنا لا نسلم أن الطواف مطلق، كيف ولو كان مطلقاً لكفى شوط واحد فإنه أدنى ما يطلق عليه اسم الطواف لغة، بل المراد الطواف الشرعي المعتبر عند الشارع، وهو مجمل في الأركان والشروط، فيقع هذا الخبر بياناً لشرطه، فلا نسخ أصلاً، فلا يلزم عليه محذور فحينئذ لا يصلح تفرع هذه الفريعة على هذا الأصل، بل الحق في الجواب أن تمثيل شيء بشيء لا يوجب في المماثلة للصلاة في اشتراط الطهارة، بل يجوز أن يكون المعنى يوجب الطواف، مثل الصلاة في الثواب في الآخرة، فلا تكلموا إلا بخير، لكن على هذا لا بد لوجوب الطهارة من غير اشتراط من دليل آخر، ولعله هنا الاحتياط في أمر العبادة فافهم
Our proof: The absolute (without the addition) indicates sufficiency absolutely, whether with the addition or free from it, because the absolute is like the general: it indicates its individuals that are with the addition or free from it on a substitution basis, and there is no preventer from it, because speech is about what has no preventer other than this addition, and it is assumed absent at the time of the absolute's existence, so it is interpreted as absolute, and it indicates that. And the restriction (by a part or condition) contradicts it, because it necessitates non-sufficiency without it. So this restriction raises a shar'i ruling, which is the sufficiency of individuals free from this restriction, and this is very apparent. Then he branched on this issue another issue and said: And because of this, and because adding a part or condition is naskh, we forbid addition by khabar wahid to a qat'i text like the Book; otherwise it would entail abrogation of the qat'i by the conjectural. If you say: You have permitted addition by mashhoor hadith even though it is conjectural, I say: We will explain its reason inshaAllah. Like purity for tawaf: we do not make it a condition such that tawaf without purity is invalid, nor is repetition required, unlike al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). His followers adhere to what al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i narrated from Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his Companions and family) said: 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer, except that you may talk in it; so whoever talks in it, let him not talk except good.' Our scholars answered, as the author indicated, by saying that Allah's statement: 'And let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House' [al-Hajj:29] is absolute, so adding purity to it and restricting its absoluteness is not permitted by this conjectural hadith. Rather the obligatory tawaf remains absolute, but we say purity is obligatory acting on this hadith, so a compensating blood sacrifice is required if he makes tawaf without wudu, but the obligation is fulfilled. Thus they said. Shaykh al-Haddad objected: We do not accept that tawaf is absolute. How so? If it were absolute, one circuit would suffice, for that is the minimum to which the name 'tawaf' applies linguistically. Rather the intent is the legally considered tawaf according to the Lawgiver, which is ambiguous in its pillars and conditions. So this hadith becomes a clarification of its condition, and thus there is no naskh at all, so no problem arises. Then the branching of this subsidiary on this principle is not valid. Rather the correct answer is that comparing one thing to another does not necessitate similarity to prayer in requiring purity; rather it may mean that tawaf is like prayer in reward in the afterlife, so speak only good. But on this, the obligation of purity must come from another proof, and perhaps here caution in matters of worship suffices. So understand.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi proof that an absolute (mutlaq) command indicates the sufficiency of any instance, including those without an added part or condition. Therefore, adding a restriction (whether part or condition) removes a shar'i ruling (the sufficiency of the unrestricted version), which is abrogation. This principle has a practical application: since adding a condition via a khabar wahid to a qat'i text would be abrogation, Hanafis do not accept the hadith about tawaf requiring wudu as a condition for validity. Instead, they interpret the hadith as either exhorting to purity (causing a blood sacrifice if omitted) or referring to reward. They respond to Shaykh al-Haddad's objection that tawaf is not absolute because the minimum of one circuit linguistically is not enough; the legal tawaf is defined by the Lawgiver. The author supports the Hanafi position that the mutlaq command in the Quran (Surah al-Hajj) is not abrogated by a zanni hadith.

Key Terms
المطلق (al-muṭlaq): A text that indicates an act without any restrictions or conditions.
الطواف (al-ṭawāf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba as part of Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, what is the consequence for someone who performs tawaf without wudu?
A) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The tawaf is valid but a blood sacrifice is required.
C) The tawaf is valid and no sacrifice is needed.
D) The tawaf is not acceptable until wudu is performed.

Key Takeaway
A mutlaq text cannot be qualified by a zanni proof; the addition would be naskh, which is impermissible without equal authority.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
6 min
زيادة الجزء أو الشرط نسخ عند الحنفية
بيان أن زيادة الجزء أو الشرط على النص القاطع تعتبر نسخاً

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that adding a part or condition to a definitive text constitutes abrogation (naskh) and explain why khabar al-wahid cannot abrogate a qat'i text.

Core Idea
Adding a part or condition to a definitive text abrogates its original ruling; therefore, it cannot be done by a probable report.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi usul principle: when a definitive text (like the Quran) is absolute (muthlaq) regarding a ruling, any addition of a part or condition (taqyid) effectively cancels that ruling for cases without the addition. Hanafis classify this as abrogation (naskh). Consequently, such addition cannot be established by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid), which is only probable (zanni), because that would abrogate a definitive text with something uncertain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the Hanafi rule: adding a part or condition to a definitive text is naskh (abrogation).
This rule applies only to qat'i texts like the Quran and mutawatir sunnah.
2
Understand the proof (talil)
Follow the author's reasoning: the absolute (muthlaq) text indicates its ruling for all individuals, whether with the addition or without. Restricting it by a part or condition contradicts this absoluteness and removes the ruling for the unrestricted cases.
The muthlaq is like the amm: it covers all instances until a clear diverting factor (sarf) appears.
3
Classify the addition as naskh
Since the taqyid removes a legal ruling (the validity of unrestricted cases), it qualifies as naskh (abrogation) in the Hanafi view.
Other schools may see it as bayan (clarification) rather than naskh.
4
Apply the consequence
Because naskh of a qat'i text requires a qat'i proof, khabar al-wahid (zanni) is insufficient.
Hence the Hanafi position: no addition to the Quran by khabar al-wahid.
5
Note the exception
The author mentions that khabar mashhur (well-known report) is permitted for addition, even though it is also zanni. This will be explained later.
The distinction between khabar wahid and mashhur in terms of strength will be clarified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لنا أن المطلق عن تلك الزيادة دل على الأجزاء مطلقاً سواء كان مع الزيادة أو مجرداً عنها لأنه كالعام يدل على أفراده التي مع الزيادة أو مجرداً عنها بدلاً وليس هناك صارف عنه، لأن الكلام فيما لا صارف غير هذه الزيادة، وهي مفروضة الانتفاء زمان وجود المطلق فيحمل على الإطلاق، ويدل عليه والتقييد بجزء أو شرط ينافيه فإنه يقتضي عدم الإجزاء بدونه فيرفع هذا التقييد حكماً شرعياً وهو إجزاء الأفراد التي هي مجردة عن هذا التقييد، وهذا ظاهر جداً، ثم فرع على هذه المسألة مسألة أخرى فقال ولهذا ولأجل أن زيادة جزء أو شرط نسخ امتنع عندنا الزيادة بخبر الواحد على القاطع كالكتاب، وإلا لزم انتساخ القاطع بالمظنون، فإن قلت : قد جوزتم الزيادة بالخبر المشهور مع أنه مظنون، قلت : سنبيّن وجهه إن شاء الله تعالى
For us: the absolute (muthlaq) without that addition indicates the parts absolutely, whether with the addition or stripped of it, because it is like the general (amm) indicating its individuals that are with the addition or stripped of it, as alternatives, and there is no diverting factor from it, because the discourse is about what has no diverting factor other than this addition, and it is assumed non-existent at the time of the existence of the absolute, so it is interpreted upon absoluteness. And it indicates this. And the restriction (taqyid) by a part or condition contradicts it, for it requires non-fulfillment without it. So this restriction removes a legal ruling, which is the validity of the individuals that are stripped of this restriction. This is very apparent. Then he derived another issue from this issue and said: and because of this, and because the addition of a part or condition is abrogation (naskh), it is prohibited for us to add by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) to a definitive text (qat'i) like the Book, otherwise that would necessitate abrogation of the definitive by the probable. If you say: you have permitted addition by the well-known report (khabar mashhur) even though it is probable, I say: we will explain its justification if God wills.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental Hanafi usul rule: adding a part (juz') or condition (shart) to a definitive text constitutes abrogation (naskh). The proof: the absolute text (muthlaq) initially establishes the ruling for all individuals, including those without the added element. Restricting it with a part or condition contradicts this absoluteness and effectively abrogates the ruling for the unrestricted cases. Therefore, such addition cannot be made by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) because that would entail abrogating a definitive text with a probable one. The author also notes that addition by a well-known report (khabar mashhur) is permitted, and this will be explained later.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): رفع حكم شرعي بدليل شرعي متأخر
زيادة (ziyada): إضافة جزء أو شرط إلى النص المطلق
مطلق (muthlaq): اللفظ الدال على الماهية من غير قيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
لماذا لا يجوز عند الحنفية زيادة جزء أو شرط على النص القاطع بخبر الواحد؟
A) لأن خبر الواحد لا يفيد العلم
B) لأن الزيادة تعتبر نسخاً للقاطع بالمظنون
C) لأن الإجماع منع ذلك
D) لأن النص القاطع لا يقبل التقييد أصلاً

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: adding a part or condition to a definitive text is naskh, and thus requires a qat'i proof, not a solitary report.

Naskh — Abrogation
advanced
6 min
The Hanafi Principle: Addition of an Obligation via Khabar Wahid is Naskh
Explaining that additions to clear Qur'anic commands via ahad hadith constitute naskh, using fiqh examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that a khabar wahid cannot add an obligation to a qati' text, and evaluate the opposing view that such addition is takhsis.

Core Idea
Adding an obligation to a clear Qur'anic command via a solitary hadith is naskh, not permissible.

This passage from Fawātih al-Rahamūt addresses a pivotal usul al-fiqh debate: can a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) add a new obligation to a ruling derived from a definitive (qati') Qur'anic text? The Hanafi school answers no—such an addition would be abrogation (naskh), not specification (takhsis) or explanation (bayan). The text uses examples from wudu and prayer to illustrate the principle and refutes counterarguments from other schools. You will learn to identify when a hadith attempts to add to a qati' text and why Hanafi methodology resists it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qati' text
Find the definitive Qur'anic ruling in the discussion—e.g., the verse of wudu (5:6), the verse of recitation (73:20), or the verse of bowing/prostration (22:77). These texts are qati' in both transmission and meaning.
The passage assumes these verses are unambiguous in their indication.
2
Identify the khabar wahid
Note the solitary hadith that seems to add an obligation—e.g., hadith of intention, hadith of basmalah, hadith of al-Fatiha, hadith of the Bedouin on i'tidal. Classify these as zanni in transmission.
The hadith of al-Fatiha is narrated by Bukhari and Muslim, but its text is also disturbed (mudtarib).
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
Determine whether the hadith proposes an addition beyond the qati' text. If the original text commands an absolute act (e.g., any recitation), requiring a specific act (e.g., al-Fatiha) is an addition. The Hanafi rule: addition to a qati' text via zanni evidence is naskh and impermissible.
This applies only when the original text is not mujmal (ambiguous); if it were, the hadith could be bayan.
4
Consider the counterarguments
Examine the opponent's claim that the hadith is bayan (explanation) or takhsis (specification). The Hanafi rebuttal: the original text is not mujmal, and the absolute (mutlaq) only indicates the common essence, not specific individuals. Without a contextual clue, the later text cannot specify.
The opponent's takhsis argument is refuted because the absolute has no generality to be restricted.
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical effect: In the Hanafi school, reciting any part of the Qur'an suffices in prayer; in the Shafi'i school, al-Fatiha is obligatory. Similarly, intention is not obligatory in wudu according to Hanafis, but it is according to Shafi'is.
The passage notes that Ibn al-Hammam considered the basmalah hadith hasan, which could establish wujub (obligation) but not rukniyya (pillar).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكثير أي ككثير من الفروع منها عدم وجوب النية والترتيب في الوضوء، لقوله عليه وآله الصلاة والسلام: : «الأعمال بالنيات رواه الشيخان وغيرهما والمواظبة على الترتيب من غير ترك قال في سفر السعادة لم يترك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الترتيب مرة. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله بوجوبهما لذلك، وكذا عدم وجوب الموالاة بالمواظبة المذكورة كما عليه مالك رضي الله عنه، وكذا عدم وجوب التسمية لقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «لا وضوء لمن لم يسم» رواه الدارقطني كما قال به أحمد رحمه الله وكذا عدم وجوب التخليل، لقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : خللوا أصابعكم كيلا تتخللها نار جهنم وذلك لأن آية الوضوء إنما تدل على أجزاء غسل الأعضاء الثلاثة الرأس مطلقاً مع مسح عن النية وغيرها مما ذكر، فلو زيد أحد هذه الأشياء لزم انتساخ القاطع بخبر الواحد، كذا قالوا: وهذا العذر صحيح فيما وراء النية، أما هي فحديث : الأعمال بالنيات مشهور به تصح الزيادة على الكتاب، بل الحق فيه أن الحديث لا يدل على اشتراط النية أصلاً في الوضوء وغيره من الوسائل. ثم إن هذا العذر إنما يكفي لعدم افتراض هذه الأمور، لكنه يجوز أن تكون واجبة، فالنية قد عرفت حالها، وأما الترتيب والموالاة فلأن الفعل لا يدل على الوجوب كما سيجيء، وليس قول يدل عليه، وأما التخليل فلثبوت الترك، وعدم نقل من نقل وضوء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم من الصحابة المعتبرين، وأما التسمية فلأن الحديث ضعيف كما بين في ،موضعه، لكن الشيخ ابن الهمام قال في فتح القدير: إنّ هذا الحديث لتكثر طرقه وكون الخلل الذي في راويه غير الفسق صار في درجة الحسن، فهو وإن لم يوجب الركنية لئلا يلزم الزيادة على الكتاب لكن ينبغي أن يثبت الوجوب، فتأمل فيه فإنه موضع تأمل، ومنها : عدم ركنية الفاتحة في الصلاة، كما قال الأئمة الثلاثة، لقول صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب رواه الشيخان لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَأَقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْءَانِ ﴾ [المزمل: ۲۰] يقتضي افتراض مطلق القراءة لما تيسر أي قدّر كان من أي سورة كانت، فجعل الفاتحة ركناً نسخ لهذا القاطع بخبر الواحد فلا يجوز، وكذا تعديل الأركان ليس ركناً، وكذا القومة بعد الركوع ، لحديث الأعرابي المخرّج في الصحيحين». و«موطأ الإمام محمد» خلافاً للأئمة الثلاثة والإمام أبي يوسف، وإلا لزم الزيادة على قوله تعالى: ﴿أَرْكَعُواْ وَاسْجُدُوا ﴾ [الحج : ۷۷] بخبر الواحد وأورد عليه أيضاً بمثل ما أن الصلاة مجملة، فيلتحق مر خبر الفاتحة وحديث الأعرابي بياناً، فلا نسخ ويمكن أن يجاب أن ركن القراءة والركوع والسجود قد ثبت بالقاطع، فلا يلحق هذان الخبران بياناً، وإنما يصيران زيادة على هذا القاطع، ثم ألحق في خبر الفاتحة ما ذكر، فإن القراءة قد فرضت مطلقة بالقاطع ولا إجمال فيه أصلاً حتى يلحق خبر الفاتحة بياناً مع أن متنه مضطرب أيضاً، فإنه قد يروي الصلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب خداج والخداج الناقص، فهذا يقتضي تحقق الصلاة مع النقصان بدونها، وأما حديث الأعرابي فإنما سيق لبيان حقيقة الصلاة، فإن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قال له : صلِّ فإنك لم تصل حين ترك التعديل، ثم بين له الأركان الصلاتية المعدلة، هي) الأمر الأصل الأول الكتاب فهو بيان قطعاً، وأما قوله تعالى : أَرْكَعُواْ وَأَسْجُدُوا ﴾ [الحج: ٧٧] فقد قيل : أريد به الصلاة من قبيل إطلاق الجزء على الكل، ولو سلم أنه على معناه فليس المراد به الركوع كيفما اتفق، فإن الركوع قبل القراءة غير معتد به وكذا السجدة الواحدة بل المراد الركوع على نحو خاص، أعني مع الشرائط، فهو مجمل باعتبار الشرائط، فيلحق حديث الأعرابي بياناً، فأذن الحق قول الإمام أبي يوسف فافهم، وههنا فروع أخرى يطول الكلام بذكرها، وإذا قد عرفت أن الزيادة مغيرة للحكم المطلق فما في) شرح (المختصر أن زيادة غسل عضو في الوضوء أو ركن في الصلاة ليس بنسخ ساقط لأن تحقق الامتثال بالأول المطلق عن غسل هذا العضو المفروض الآن أو الركن المفروض الآن لم يبق كما عرفت (بل) الامتثال حينئذ (بالكل) فقط لا غير (فتدبر) منكرو كون الزيادة نسخا (قالوا الزيادة (تخصيص) للمزيد عليه من الأصل (لأنه أهون) من النسخ لكونه ،إبطالاً، وهذا بيان قلنا : المطلق لا يدل إلا على الماهية من حيث هي * أي على أمر صالح لأن يوجد في كل فرد سواء كان ماهية مطلقة، كالغسل المفهوم في بالوضوء أو الفرد المبهم كرقبة فلا ينافي ما مر في فصل المطلق والمقيد والتخصيص فرع الدلالة على المشخصات لفظاً كما مر) يعني أن التخصيص إنما يكون إذا كان هناك دلالة على المشخصات المعينه والمطلق إنما يدل على القدر المشترك، ولا دلالة للعام على الخاص بإحدى الدلالات وليس ههنا قرينة صارفة عن القدر المشترك إلى المشخصات، إذ غير النص الدال على الزيادة مفروض الانتفاء، وهذا النص متراخ عنه معدوم في زمان التكلم فلا دلالة له على المشخصات، ولم يرد به أن التخصيص، إنما يكون في العام وهو فرع الدلالة على العموم، ولا عموم في المطلق لدلالته على الماهية حتى يرد عليه أنه لم يرد المستدل بالتخصيص قصر العام بل القصر المطلق على طريق الدفع والحاصل أن الدفع أهون من الرفع فتدبر
And many, meaning like many of the branches, among them: the non-obligation of intention (niyyah) and sequence (tartīb) in wuḍū', due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Actions are by intentions' – narrated by al-Bukhārī and Muslim and others – and the continuous practice of sequence without omission. It is said in Safar al-Sa'ādah: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, never omitted the sequence once. And al-Shāfi'ī, may Allah have mercy on him, said they are obligatory because of that. Likewise the non-obligation of continuity (muwālāh) due to the mentioned continuous practice, as is the position of Mālik, may Allah be pleased with him. Likewise the non-obligation of reciting the basmalah due to his saying, peace be upon him and his family and companions: 'No wuḍū' for one who does not mention [Allah's name]' – narrated by al-Dāraquṭnī – as is the position of Aḥmad, may Allah have mercy on him. Likewise the non-obligation of khilāl (passing fingers through beard/hair) due to his saying, peace be upon him and his family and companions: 'Khallilū aṣābi'akum [pass water through your fingers] lest the fire of Hell penetrates between them.' This is because the verse of wuḍū' only indicates the parts: washing the three limbs and wiping the head absolutely, with no mention of intention and others mentioned. So if one of these things were added, it would necessitate abrogation of the definitive (qāṭi') by a solitary report (khabar al-wāḥid). Thus they said. And this excuse is valid for matters other than intention. As for that, the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' is well-known, by which the addition to the Book is validated. Rather the truth is that the hadith does not indicate the condition of intention at all in wuḍū' and other means. Then this excuse suffices for not assuming these matters as obligatory, but it is possible that they are wājib. The case of intention is known. As for sequence and continuity, because the action does not indicate obligation as will come, and there is no statement indicating it. As for khilāl, because the omission is established, and the failure of reliable Companions to transmit the wuḍū' of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him and his family and companions, [with khilāl]. As for the basmalah, because the hadith is weak as explained in its place. However, Shaykh Ibn al-Hammām said in Fatḥ al-Qadīr: 'This hadith, due to the multiplicity of its chains and the fact that the defect in its narrator is not fisq, has reached the rank of ḥasan. So although it does not necessitate pillar-status (rukniyya) to avoid adding upon the Book, it should establish obligation (wujūb).' So reflect, for it is a place of reflection. And among them: the non-pillar-status of al-Fātiḥa in prayer, as the three imāms said, due to his saying, peace be upon him and his family and companions: 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fātiḥa of the Book' – narrated by al-Bukhārī and Muslim – because His saying, exalted: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' (al-Muzzammil 73:20) necessitates the obligation of absolute recitation of what is easy, meaning whatever part from any sūra. So making al-Fātiḥa a pillar would abrogate this definitive (qāṭi') by a solitary report, which is not permissible. Likewise, standing upright (i'tidāl) of the pillars is not a pillar, likewise the upright standing (qawma) after bowing, due to the hadith of the Bedouin recorded in the two Ṣaḥīḥs and the Muwaṭṭa' of Imam Muḥammad, contrary to the three imāms and Imam Abū Yūsuf. Otherwise it would necessitate adding upon His saying, exalted: 'Bow and prostrate' (al-Ḥajj 22:77) by a solitary report. It was also objected to by what is similar: that prayer is mujmal, so the report of al-Fātiḥa and the hadith of the Bedouin attach as explanation (bayān), so there is no abrogation. It is possible to answer that the pillar of recitation, bowing, and prostration are established by a definitive text, so these two reports cannot attach as explanation; rather they become an addition upon this definitive text. Then to the report of al-Fātiḥa, what was mentioned was attached, for recitation was prescribed absolutely by a definitive text and there is no ambiguity (ijmāl) in it at all such that the report of al-Fātiḥa could attach as explanation, especially since its text is also disturbed. For it is sometimes narrated: 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fātiḥa of the Book; it is deficient (khadāj),' and al-khadāj means deficient. This implies that prayer is realized with deficiency without it. As for the hadith of the Bedouin, it was stated to explain the reality of prayer, for the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him and his family and companions, said to him: 'Pray, for you have not prayed when you left out the i'tidāl (posture of standing).' Then he explained to him the adjusted pillars of prayer. (This is) the command; the first origin is the Book, so it is a definitive explanation. As for His saying, exalted: 'Bow and prostrate' (al-Ḥajj 22:77), it has been said: It is intended for prayer, from the category of applying the part to the whole. And if it is conceded that it is in its literal sense, what is meant is not bowing absolutely however it occurs, for bowing before recitation is not considered, nor is a single prostration. Rather what is meant is bowing in a specific manner, i.e., with conditions. So it is mujmal with respect to the conditions, so the hadith of the Bedouin attaches as explanation. Therefore the truth is the saying of Imam Abū Yūsuf, so understand. And here are other branches which would be lengthy to mention. And when you have known that the addition changes the absolute ruling, what is in the commentary of al-Mukhtaṣar: 'That adding a limb in wuḍū' or a pillar in prayer is not abrogation due to cessation, because the realization of compliance with the first absolute [ruling] free from washing this limb now prescribed or the pillar now prescribed did not remain, as you have known. Rather the compliance then is with the whole only, not other.' So reflect. Those who deny that addition is abrogation said: 'Addition is specification (takhṣīṣ) of the original's object of addition, because it is easier than abrogation, since that is nullification.' And this is an explanation. We said: The absolute (muṭlaq) only indicates the essence in itself, i.e., upon a thing suitable to exist in every individual, whether it is an absolute essence like washing understood in wuḍū' or an indeterminate individual like a slave. This does not contradict what passed in the chapter of absolute and restricted. And specification is a branch of indication upon specified matters verbally, as passed. Meaning that specification only occurs when there is an indication upon specified individual matters. The absolute only indicates the common aspect, and there is no indication of the general upon the particular by any of the indications. And here there is no contextual clue (qarīna) diverting from the common aspect to the specified individuals, since other than the text indicating the addition is assumed absent. And this text is temporally distant from it, non-existent at the time of utterance, so it has no indication upon the specified individuals. And it is not intended by it that specification only occurs in the general, and it is a branch of indication upon generality, and there is no generality in the absolute because it indicates the essence, such that it might be objected that the proponent did not intend by 'specification' the restriction of the general, but rather the restriction of the absolute in the way of repulsion (daf'). The gist is that repulsion is easier than lifting, so reflect.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage deals with a key principle in Hanafi uṣūl: whether an obligation added to a clear Qur'anic ruling by a solitary hadith (khabar wāḥid) can be accepted without it being considered abrogation (naskh) of the Qur'an. The text begins by listing several well-known examples from fiqh: the non-obligation of intention (niyyah), sequence (tartīb), continuity (muwālāh), basmalah, and khilāl in wuḍū', and the non-pillar status of al-Fātiḥa, i'tidāl, and qawma in prayer. In each case, the proponents argue that making these required would contradict a definitive Qur'anic command. For example, the verse 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' demands absolute recitation—any part of the Qur'an suffices—so requiring al-Fātiḥa specifically would abrogate this absolute command. Similarly, the verse 'Bow and prostrate' (al-Ḥajj 22:77) demands simple bowing and prostration without the additional conditions of specific postures. The Hanafi position is that such additions cannot be made by a solitary report because they would abrogate a definitive (qāṭi') text. The passage then addresses counterarguments: that the reports could be considered explanatory (bayān) of an ambiguous text, or that the additions are merely specifications (takhṣīṣ) rather than abrogation. The text refutes these: for the Fātiḥa example, the verse of recitation is not ambiguous (mujmal) because it clearly states 'what is easy' and does not require a specific type. The claim of specification fails because the absolute (muṭlaq) only indicates the common essence, not particular individuals, and without a contextual clue (qarīna) diverting to specifics, addition remains abrogation. The passage also notes the opinion of Ibn al-Hammām that the basmalah hadith is ḥasan and could establish wujūb, but not rukniyya. The conclusion is that additions to clear texts are not permissible via khabar wāḥid, and the truth is with Imam Abū Yūsuf's position regarding the i'tidāl. The passage ultimately defends the Hanafi methodology of prioritizing definitive texts over solitary reports to preserve the integrity of Qur'anic commands.

Key Terms
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later textual evidence, applicable when a later ruling replaces an earlier one.
زيادة (ziyāda): Adding an extra obligation or condition to a ruling derived from a definitive text.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A solitary report (hadith ahad) that does not reach the level of tawātur.
قاطع (qāṭi'): A text that is definitive in both transmission (thubūt) and meaning (dalāla), such as a clear Qur'anic verse or mutawātir hadith.
بيان (bayān): Explanation or clarification of an ambiguous (mujmal) text, which is permissible and not considered naskh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi uṣūl principle discussed in the passage, why is it not permissible to make reciting Sūrat al-Fātiḥa a pillar (rukn) of prayer based on the hadith 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Fātiḥa'?
A) Because the hadith is weak
B) Because the Qur'anic command 'Recite what is easy from the Qur'an' is a qāṭi' text and making al-Fātiḥa a requirement would abrogate that command via a solitary report
C) Because the hadith is abrogated
D) Because the Companions disagreed on the matter

Key Takeaway
A khabar wāḥid cannot add an obligation to a qāṭi' Qur'anic ruling; doing so constitutes naskh and is impermissible.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
6 min
The Ruling on Removing a Part or Condition from an Obligation and Its Effect on the Remaining Act
Discussing the consensus that removing a part/condition is naskh, and the dispute over the remaining act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on whether removing a part or condition from an obligation abrogates the remainder, and explain the proof based on the necessary need for new evidence.

Core Idea
Removing a part/condition abrogates only that element; the remainder is not automatically abrogated.

In this passage, the author discusses an important usul principle: when a legislative text removes a part or condition from a previously established obligation, what happens to the rest of the obligation? The Hanafi school holds that the removal does not abrogate the remainder, contrary to some other views. We will analyse the consensus, the dispute, and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the consensus
Recognise that all scholars agree that removing a part or condition is abrogation (naskh) for that specific removed element. This is based on the linguistic fact that it is a lifting (raf') of a previous ruling.
The consensus covers both parts and conditions — there is no disagreement here.
2
Distinguish the dispute
The real disagreement is whether the same removal also constitutes abrogation for the remainder of the obligation (the worship or act after the removal). Some say yes, some say no. The Hanafi chosen view is that it does not.
Note that 'Abd al-Jabbār tries to separate part from condition, but the author rejects that.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof
If the removal abrogated the remainder, the remainder would need a new evidence (dalīl) to become obligatory again, because the original evidence would be lifted. Without new evidence, the ruling would be baseless — an impossibility by consensus. Therefore the remainder is not automatically abrogated.
The proof is a logical necessity: a ruling without evidence is invalid.
4
Critique the opposing distinction
'Abd al-Jabbār's claim (that removal of a part abrogates the whole, but removal of a condition does not) is deemed arbitrary. The author clarifies that the dispute is about the remainder, and both part and condition are external to the remainder, so no distinction applies.
The condition, though external, is still a requirement; its removal does not affect the core act's existence.
5
Apply the thamarah (practical consequence)
In practice, if a required element (e.g., standing in prayer) is removed, the prayer obligation continues without that element. According to the opposing view, the entire prayer would be lifted until a new text re-imposes it.
The Hanafi view preserves the continuity of obligations unless explicitly abrogated overall.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما نقص جزء أو شرط من العبادة وغيرها من الواجبات (فنسخ له) أي لذلك الجزء والشرط المنقوص (اتفاقاً) لصدق الرفع هناك (وهل هو ) أي التنقيص نسخ (لها) أي للعبادة يعني الباقي منها (فالمختار) عند المصنف (لا) أي عدم كونه مسخاً (وقيل: نعم) هو نسخ، وهو الأشبه، قال الإمام فخر الإسلام، كما أن التقييد بعد الإطلاق نسخ كذلك الإطلاق بعد التقييد (و) قال (عبد الجبار) المعتزلي (في) نقص (الجزء نعم) هو نسخ (و) قال (في) نقصان الشرط: (لا أي ليس هو نسخاً، وظاهر هذا الفرق لما كان تحكماً محضاً، قال: ولعله زعم أن النزاع في نسخ المجموع ففصل) فإن انتفاء الجزء يوجب انتفاء الكل وأما انتفاء شرطية الشرط فلا يضر بقاء حقيقة المجموع، لأنه لم يتغير شيء من أركانه (وليس كذلك أي كما زعم (بل) النزاع (نسخ الباقي بعد النقصان، وحينئذ لا فرق بين الشرط والجزء أيضاً كان شرطاً للباقي، فإنه خارج عنه، واعتداده موقوف عليه فافهم لنا : لو كان التنقيص المذكور (نسخاً للباقي لافتقر إلى دليل لإيجاب الباقي، لأن الدليل الدال عليه قد ارتفع بالنسخ، فلو لم يحتج إلى دليل (آخر) لثبت الحكم من غير دليل (وهو باطل اتفاقاً) ولعلك تقول : لعل النص الدال على التنقيص يدل على بقاء الباقي، كيف لا والقصر والنقصان وأمثاله إنما يدل على بقاء
As for the removal of a part or condition from the worship and other obligations, it is abrogation (naskh) for it, i.e., for that specific removed part or condition, by consensus, because lifting (raf') applies there. And is it, i.e., the reduction (tanqīṣ), abrogation for it, i.e., for the worship, meaning the remainder of it? The chosen view according to the author is no, i.e., it is not abrogation for the remainder. And it was said: Yes, it is abrogation, and it is the more akin. Imam Fakhr al-Islām said: Just as restriction after absoluteness is abrogation, similarly absoluteness after restriction is abrogation. And 'Abd al-Jabbār al-Mu'tazilī said regarding removal of a part: Yes, it is abrogation; and he said regarding removal of a condition: No, it is not abrogation. It appears that this distinction is pure arbitrariness. He (the author) said: Perhaps he assumed that the dispute concerns the abrogation of the whole, so he made a distinction. For the negation of a part necessitates the negation of the whole, whereas the negation of the conditionality of a condition does not harm the remaining reality of the whole, because nothing of its pillars has changed. But it is not as he assumed. Rather the dispute concerns the abrogation of the remainder after the reduction. In that case, there is no difference between condition and part. The condition is also external to the remainder, and its consideration is dependent upon the remainder. So understand. Our proof: If the mentioned reduction were abrogation of the remainder, it would require a separate evidence to obligate the remainder, because the evidence that indicated it would have been lifted by the abrogation. So if it did not need another evidence, the ruling would be established without evidence, which is invalid by consensus. And perhaps you might say: Perchance the text indicating the reduction also indicates the remaining of the remainder. How not? For shortening (qaṣr) and reduction (nuqsān) and their likes only indicate the remaining of the remainder...
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal effect of removing (naqṣ) a part or condition from an act of worship or other obligation. The text first establishes that the removal itself is considered abrogation (naskh) for that removed part or condition by consensus, because it is a lifting (raf') of the previous obligation. The disagreement is whether this removal also constitutes abrogation for the remaining part of the act. The author (the commentator) states that the chosen view is that it does not abrogate the remainder; however, some scholars held that it does. Imam Fakhr al-Islām compares it to the case of restriction after absoluteness being abrogation (a principle found in uṣūl), and equally absoluteness after restriction is abrogation. Then the text critiques the view of 'Abd al-Jabbār al-Mu'tazilī, who distinguished between removal of a part (which he said is abrogation of the whole) and removal of a condition (which he said is not abrogation of the whole). The author argues that this distinction is arbitrary, because the dispute is about whether the reduction is abrogation for the remainder, and in that context, there is no difference between a part and a condition. Both are external to the remainder. The text then provides the Hanafi proof: if the reduction were abrogation for the remainder, then the remainder would require a new evidence for its obligation, because the original evidence is lifted. Without it, the ruling would be baseless. Conversely, if the text indicating reduction also implies the remainder's obligation, then it is not abrogation for the remainder but merely a modification. The text is cut off, but the argument continues.

Key Terms
نقص (naqṣ): Removal or reduction of a part or condition from a legal obligation.
تنقيص (tanqīṣ): The act of reducing or taking away a part or condition; the process of removal.
رفع (raf'): Lifting of a legal ruling; the essence of naskh.
باقي (bāqī): The remainder of the worship or obligation after removal of a part or condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consensus regarding the removal (naqṣ) of a part or condition from an obligation according to this passage?
A) It is abrogation of the entire obligation
B) It is abrogation of only the removed part/condition
C) It is not abrogation at all
D) It is abrogation of the remainder

Key Takeaway
Removing a part or condition from an obligation does not automatically abrogate the remainder; the remainder continues to be obligatory unless new evidence lifts it.

Naskh — Abrogation
