The address of Musa (peace be upon him) commanded us to judge by what was in the law of Musa, so his law is obligatory to follow. I say: we do not accept that he was obligated by the law of Musa (peace be upon him); rather, he was commanded by the revelation that was sent down and in which the obligation of judging was commanded. Perhaps the non-recited revelation in his regard (upon him and his family and companions be blessings and peace) agreed with the recited revelation that came concerning Musa, so obligation to follow his law does not necessarily follow (understand). And it is not far to say: suppose the command to judge was by non-recited revelation—indeed it is apparent—but he (upon him and his family be blessings and peace) mentioned the recited revelation with which Musa was addressed as support and strengthening. If it were not a proof, why the support? For supporting with something not a proof, rather something forbidden to act upon, is not befitting his station; rather it is not valid from a rational person. So proof is necessary, and obligation to follow it is necessary. (And) he argued: secondly, with verses that command following the previous prophets—peace be upon our Prophet and his family and companions and them—such as His saying: 'He has prescribed for you the religion which He enjoined upon Nuh' (Shura 42:13), and His saying: 'Follow the religion of Ibrahim, a hanif, and he was not of the polytheists' (Nahl 16:123), and His saying: 'So follow their guidance' (An'am 6:90). (And it is answered) that the following commanded is in matters of belief and the five universals: preservation of religion, intellect, life, lineage, and wealth, and it is not general because necessarily some of them are abrogated absolutely. The opponents said: (first) if the obligation by the law of those before us were valid, it would have been mentioned by Mu'adh and it was not mentioned in the hadith of Mu'adh and he (upon him and his family and companions be blessings and peace) approved it. We say: he did not mention it because the Book encompasses it, so there is no need for mention; the necessary connection is denied. And the Book's encompassing is because the stories of Allah are a condition for the obligation of following it according to us. It is better to say: because the Book and Sunnah encompass it. And the answer may be formulated: the Book encompasses the Torah, Injil, and others because they are written. But making it far from the apparent meaning is against the understood meaning, for the understood from 'Kitab Allah' in the custom of the Companions until now is the noble Quran. (Or) he did not mention it because it is very little, and he only mentioned what is the source of most rulings. (And) they said: (secondly) there is consensus that our sharia abrogates the previous sharias, and obligation by the abrogated is forbidden. (We say) our sharia abrogates what contradicts it from rulings, not absolutely—like all of them such that none are proof—like qisas and the hadd of zina and others, for they are confirmed and not abrogated. (And) they said: (thirdly) he used to wait for revelation when an incident occurred, and he never referred to them to know its ruling. If their law were a proof, he would have ruled by it and not waited, and he would have referred to them to know the ruling. If you say: he did refer to them concerning stoning and ruled by what is in the Torah. He said: (as for stoning) by referring to them, it was to refute them because they claimed that the ruling of stoning is not in the Torah. (We say) the waiting and leaving off acting by the previous law in what is known through a valid path—which is revelation that it is a previous law, or tawatur that it is verified—is denied; rather, he acted as in the fast of Ashura. (As for lack of reference) to them, it is due to their distortion of the Book and their lying against Allah, so their statements are not trustworthy. So understand.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute on the bindingness (hujjiyyah) of the laws of previous prophets (shari' man qablana). It presents the proponent's arguments and the Hanafi response. The passage first discusses the example of Prophet Musa (AS) where the Prophet Muhammad (SAW) was commanded to judge by the law of Musa. The commentator argues that this command was not because the law of Musa is binding per se, but because the revelation agreed with it. Then he rebuts the argument that the Quran commands following previous prophets; he limits it to beliefs and the five necessities (daruriyyat). Then the opponents give three objections: (1) It was not mentioned in the hadith of Mu'adh; answer: the Quran encompasses it or it was too rare. (2) Our sharia abrogates all previous; answer: only what contradicts, not all. (3) The Prophet waited for revelation, not referring to previous laws; answer: in known cases he did act (like Ashura), and non-reference was due to distortion. The passage maintains that previous sharias are binding only if confirmed by our revelation, not absolutely.

Key Terms
شرع من قبلنا (shar'u man qablana): The revealed laws of prophets before Prophet Muhammad (SAW).
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a ruling by a later revealed ruling.
وحي غير متلو (wahi ghayr matluww): Non-recited revelation, i.e., inspiration not part of the Quran (e.g., hadith qudsi or sunnah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why did the Prophet not refer to previous scriptures for rulings on every new incident?
A) Because previous scriptures were completely abrogated
B) Because he was commanded to wait for new revelation
C) Because the previous scriptures were distorted and unreliable
D) Because he knew all rulings by heart

Key Takeaway
For Hanafis, the sharia of previous prophets is a proof only when confirmed by our own revelation, not as an independent source.

Naskh — Abrogation
intermediate
6 min
Definition and Reality of Ta'arud in Hanafi Usul
Defines ta'arud and asserts its unreality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ta'arud, explain why true conflict does not occur among valid legal proofs, and identify the two causes of apparent conflict.

Core Idea
Ta'arud is only apparent—valid proofs never truly contradict; otherwise, Shari'ah would be inconsistent.

This lesson introduces the concept of ta'arud (conflict between evidences) in Hanafi legal theory. The author defines it as the mutual repulsion of two proofs, but immediately emphasizes that such conflict is not real among sound legal evidences. Instead, any perceived contradiction arises from either ignorance of chronology (leading to abrogation) or error in interpretation. Understanding this principle is crucial for resolving apparent disagreements in the sources.

Guided Path
1
Define ta'arud linguistically and technically
Identify that ta'arud means mutual opposition. Note that the definition includes conditions of unity in time, ruling, place etc.
The term 'tadafu'' (mutual repulsion) highlights the apparent push-and-pull between two proofs.
2
Understand why true conflict is impossible
Reason: if both proofs are valid and their premises correct in reality, their conclusions must be true and consistent; contradictory conclusions would imply contradictory truths, which cannot coexist. This holds for both qat'i and zanni proofs.
This is a logical argument (imtina' al-tanqud).
3
Distinguish apparent from real conflict
Conflict only appears at first glance due to two factors: ignorance of historical sequence (jahl bi al-tarikh) or error in understanding (khata' fi al-fahm).
This leads to methods of resolution: naskh (abrogation) and tarij (preponderance).
4
Apply the principle to a hypothetical
Suppose two hadiths seem to contradict. Instead of assuming a flaw, a mujtahid checks chronological order and meaning; if one is later, it may abrogate; if both are from same time, they may be reconciled via interpretation.
This aligns with Hanafi emphasis on consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : في التعارض، وهو تدافع الحجتين ، ولا يتحقق إلا بوحدات من الزمان والحكم والمحل وغير ذلك (ولا يكون) في الحجج الشرعية (في نفس الأمر ، وإلا لزم التناقض فإن الحجج الشرعية فلا بد من إنتاجها في نفس أمر إن كانت صحيحة المقدمات في نفس الأمر، وقد فرضت كذلك، فيلزم وقوع النتائج المتناقضة في نفس الأمر، سواء كان (قطعاً) كما إذا كان الحجتان مقطوعتين (أو ظناً) كما إذا كانتا مظنونتين بل يتصور) التعارض (ظاهراً) في بادىء الرأي للجهل بالتاريخ أو الخطأ في فهم
Chapter: On Conflict (Ta'arud), which is the mutual repulsion of two proofs. It is not realized except with unity in time, ruling, place, and other factors. (And it does not exist) in the case of legal proofs (in actual reality, otherwise it would entail contradiction. For legal proofs must produce results in actual fact if their premises are correct in actual fact, and they are assumed to be so. Thus contradictory results would necessarily occur in reality, whether the proofs are (definitive) as when both are definitive, or (speculative) as when both are speculative. Rather, conflict is (imaginable) (apparently) at first glance due to ignorance of the historical sequence or error in understanding.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This short chapter begins the discussion of ta'arud (conflict) between legal proofs. The author defines ta'arud as the mutual opposition of two proofs (hujjatayn) such that they appear to lead to contradictory rulings. However, he immediately clarifies that true conflict cannot actually occur among valid legal proofs from the Shari'ah, because if both proofs are genuine and their premises sound, they must produce consistent results. Any apparent contradiction is only superficial, arising from either ignorance of the chronological order (which proof came later and abrogated the other) or from misunderstanding the correct interpretation of one or both proofs. This applies whether the proofs are definitive (qat'i) or speculative (zanni). Thus, the mujtahid must seek to reconcile or determine precedence. The passage is cut off but sets the foundational principle for the science of conflict resolution.

Key Terms
التعارض (al-ta'arud): The apparent opposition between two legal proofs (hujaj) that seems to lead to contradictory rulings; in reality, true conflict does not occur because valid proofs cannot contradict each other in actual fact.
الحجج الشرعية (al-hujaj al-shar'iyyah): Legal proofs derived from the Shari'ah, such as the Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, which are assumed to be consistent in their real import.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why can true conflict (ta'arud) not occur among legal proofs in reality?
A) Because all legal proofs are speculative and can be interpreted differently.
B) Because if the premises of both proofs are correct, they must produce consistent results; otherwise, contradiction would entail.
C) Because legal proofs are only valid if they come from the same source.
D) Because conflict only occurs between definitive proofs, not speculative ones.

Key Takeaway
True conflict (ta'arud) does not occur among valid legal proofs; any appearance of contradiction is due to ignorance of chronology or misinterpretation.
